Current Affairs Commentary

The European Situation and the Memel Question

— Wei

The prelude to World War II can be said to have already begun. In recent months, diplomats from peace-loving countries in Geneva have been striving for a peaceful resolution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. The first gunshot on the East African front has finally awakened them from their illusions. They have currently abandoned hope for peace and are seeking to join forces to confront the current enemy. Britain is requesting maritime assistance from France to counter Italy, and France has also requested Britain to guarantee peace in Central Europe to prevent Germany from moving south. Other politicians with great ambitions are embarking on the path of war, concentrating their minds and strength on military affairs to achieve immediate victory. Those who have not embarked on the path of war are maneuvering diplomatically to achieve future victory. Therefore, on one hand, some countries recognize this as a matter of life and death, while on the other hand, some countries see this as a good opportunity to expand their territory and gain rights.

In Southern Europe, Italy has unleashed the surging waves of war, while in Northern Europe, Germany is quietly awaiting the opportunity to achieve its goal of fishing in troubled waters. As Italy is currently preoccupied and unable to pay attention to Austria-Hungary, which it has always regarded as off-limits, the National Socialist Party believes that a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity has arrived for Germany. We are once again seeing German diplomats active in Eastern Europe. The signing of the German-Polish ten-year non-aggression treaty has transformed Poland from a French satellite into a German "partner." Now, Hitler is taking advantage of Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös's visit to Germany to conduct secret negotiations and reportedly plans to conclude a five-year non-aggression treaty with Austria. The purpose of this is undoubtedly to organize a German-Polish-Austrian-Hungarian bloc to counter the Central European Little Entente group and the Eastern European Baltic group – Lithuania, Latvia, Estonia.

The National Socialist Party's view of the Baltic Sea as its own possession has long been evident in the plans of the National Socialist Party spokesman, Rosenberg. Not only are National Socialist propaganda pamphlets frequently distributed within these three countries, but the activities of National Socialist Party members often threaten the current governments of the three countries. Therefore, these three countries have undergone a transformation since the National Socialist Party came to power, shifting their fear from the Soviet Union to Germany. To defend against their common enemy, the Baltic Entente was signed. The main content of the agreement is to stipulate that the three countries should have a common diplomatic position and that the three foreign ministers should meet once a year to decide on major foreign policies to deal with external aggression. However, these provisions are fundamentally political rather than military. If the National Socialist Party implements its "Eastern Policy," it is questionable whether these three countries can deal with it consistently and whether the three countries have the strength to deal with it. Germany's wait-and-see approach has now become an open secret, especially evident in its attitude towards the Memel question. Germany's particular hostility towards Lithuania has its own special reasons. However, its main purpose is still to expand its territory. Therefore, any country that hinders its ambition is the country it hates. Lithuania is just the first to bear the brunt, and Memel is just the beginning.

Memel became a focal point for the National Socialist Party because Memel originally belonged to Germany before the war and was governed by the League of Nations after the war. In 1923, Memel was occupied by Lithuania. In 1924, representatives from Britain, Japan, Italy, and France met in Paris and recognized Lithuania's sovereignty. However, at the same time, they granted Memel a considerable degree of autonomy. The area has a parliament, with members elected by the local population, and a governor, appointed by Lithuania. The governor and parliament often clash, and the local people's feelings towards Lithuania are extremely negative. This phenomenon provides Germany with an excuse to oppose Lithuania. Therefore, after the Saar plebiscite in the spring of this year, Germany had the slogan of holding a plebiscite in Memel to return to Germany, following the Saar example. In fact, the status of Memel should not be equated with that of the Saar. However, in the minds of the Germans, they have no time to consider this. Taking Memel for themselves is their only goal. The National Socialist Party's aim in this local parliamentary election is to win more seats in parliament and overthrow Lithuanian rule in one fell swoop. The election has now ended, but the results are still uncertain. The Lithuanian officials cannot sit idly by and watch their territory fall into the hands of others. In Germany, they believe that Memel's return to Germany is a foregone conclusion. There is no possibility of compromise between the two sides on this point. The international situation has made it difficult for countries such as Italy, France, Britain, and Japan, which guarantee Memel's return to Lithuania, to avoid being drawn into the vortex and have no time to care about Lithuania's suffering. Therefore, the future of the Memel question is bleak. Moreover, this is not only a problem for Lithuania alone or the Baltic countries, but also a problem concerning world peace.

British Royal Family's Chinese Antiquities: Participate in Exhibition for Public Viewing

(London) The British King and Queen today sent 46 pieces of Chinese antiquities from their collection to the Chinese Art Exhibition, which will be displayed for public appreciation on the opening day, November 28. Among them is a set of steel ware, which was given to Queen Victoria of England by the Chinese Emperor in 1887. (4th Reuters Telegram)

Mussolini Meets with German Ambassador: Discusses Assistance Issues

(Rome) Prime Minister Mussolini met with the German Ambassador to Italy, von Hassell, today to discuss whether Italy could obtain assistance from Germany if other countries decide to implement sanctions. Mussolini inquired about Germany's attitude towards this. The German Ambassador replied that he would seek instructions from the Berlin government, but he personally believed that Italy could rest assured. (4th National Telegram)

Italo-Abyssinian Dispute Diary (From the Walwal Incident in 1934 to the Outbreak of War on October 4, 1935)

1914

December 5 Italian and Abyssinian troops clashed in the Walwal area on the Italo-Abyssinian border.

December 16 Abyssinia submitted an application to the League of Nations.

1935

January 16 Abyssinia formally filed a complaint with the League of Nations based on Article 11 of the League Covenant.

February 9 Ten thousand Italian troops set sail for East Africa.

March 17 Abyssinia filed another complaint with the League of Nations.

May 24 The League of Nations Council convened and resolved to establish an arbitration committee for the Italo-Abyssinian dispute in the Walwal incident.

June 6 The arbitration committee convened in Milan.

June 24 British representative Eden visited Italy and proposed a compromise to Mussolini, without result.

June 25 The arbitration committee convened in The Hague, Netherlands.

July 4 Abyssinia invoked the Kellogg-Briand Pact and requested mediation from the United States; the United States did not respond.

July 9 The arbitration committee convened in The Hague and broke down.

July 16 Two hundred thousand Italian troops had entered East Africa.

July 18 The Abyssinian Emperor delivered a speech to the National Assembly to inspire the people.

July 31

To August 5 The League of Nations Council convened a special session and resolved: (1) to convene a conference of Great Britain, France, and Italy to discuss a peace plan; (2) to convene a Council meeting on September 4; (3) to appoint a fifth arbitrator.

August 16

To August 18 The conference of Great Britain, France, and Italy convened in Paris. The compromise proposed by Great Britain and France was rejected by Italy, and the conference broke down.

August 22 Great Britain convened an emergency cabinet meeting, leaning towards sanctions against Italy.

August 28 France convened an emergency cabinet meeting, opposing sanctions against Italy.

August 31 The Abyssinian Emperor granted oil rights to the British-American joint venture East African Plantation Company.

September 1 British representative Eden met with French Premier Laval.

September 4 The League of Nations Council convened, and the Italian representative declared that they reserved the right to act freely.

September 5 The League of Nations Council resolved to organize a five-nation committee consisting of Great Britain, France, Poland, Spain, and Turkey to study ways to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute.

The Abyssinian representative, Mr. Siss, delivered a speech at the Council meeting, criticizing Italy. The Italian representative walked out.

September 6 Laval advocated for the demilitarization of the Abyssinian gendarmerie, to be commanded by British and Italian officers, in order to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute.

September 8 The Italian Navy held large-scale maneuvers between Sicily and the African coast. The Abyssinian Emperor's court decided on the limits of major concessions to Italy.

September 10 Abyssinia formally rejected Italy's dispatch of troops to protect the embassy.

British Foreign Secretary Hoare stated Britain's attitude towards the Italo-Abyssinian dispute at the League of Nations General Assembly.

French Ambassador to Great Britain Corbin inquired of Great Britain whether Britain would support League of Nations sanctions with effective means.

September 13 Italian troops in Libya concentrated on the border with Egypt.

The Abyssinian government sent a document to the League of Nations refuting Italy's memorandum accusing Abyssinia of preparing for war.

September 15 Italian troop concentrations threatened Egypt, and British-Italian relations became strained.

September 16 The League of Nations Five-Nation Committee report concealed matters and expanded the Paris Conference's recommendations.

September 17 The League of Nations Five-Nation Committee convened to consider mediation proposals.

September 18 The Five-Nation Committee's suggestions were communicated to the Italian and Abyssinian representatives.

Laval and Aloisi personally returned to Rome to confer with the Prime Minister.

September 19 The British fleet concentrated in the Mediterranean.

Mussolini expressed that it was difficult to accept the Five-Nation Committee's recommendations.

September 20 Abyssinia accepted the Five-Nation Committee's recommendations.

September 21 Italy rejected the Five-Nation Committee's recommendations.

September 22 Britain earnestly hoped that Italy would submit a counter-proposal.

September 23 Great Britain and Italy mutually guaranteed that naval and electrical activities were not hostile.

Italian troops continued to sail to East Africa.

September 24 Greece protested to Italy about Italian warships entering harbors.

British Ambassador to the League of Nations Hoare visited Mussolini again.

The Five-Nation Committee's report was completed.

September 25 The Five-Nation Committee's report was released.

Describing the failure of mediation.

The British Cabinet resolved that Mediterranean defenses could not be neglected.

Italy hoped to have Abyssinia as a mandated territory.

September 26 The League of Nations Council resolved to form a thirteen-nation committee consisting of Great Britain, France, Russia, Abyssinia, Argentina, Spain, Australia, Turkey, Romania, Poland, Portugal, Sweden, Mexico, Chile to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute.

Great Britain, France, and Russia expressed their firm adherence to the League Covenant.

September 27 The Thirteen-Nation Committee held its first meeting.

British politician Churchill urged Italy to reconsider.

Italian troops continued to sail to East Africa.

September 28 Abyssinia celebrated the end of the rainy season.

Tensions escalated in the Mediterranean as Great Britain and Italy deployed defenses.

Observers in Geneva speculated that Italy was seeking an extra-League solution.

September 30 19,000 Italian troops continued to sail to East Africa.

The British Ambassador to France reiterated the full text of the public statement, supporting the League Covenant.

France was completely satisfied.

Abyssinia issued a general mobilization order.

The Thirteen-Nation Committee convened.

October 1 British naval and air forces conducted large-scale maneuvers outside Egyptian ports.

The Italian Ambassador visited the British Foreign Office. Britain stated that it would not negotiate externally.

October 2 The Italian Fascist Party held a general mobilization exercise.

Italian consuls stationed in Abyssinia were ordered to leave the country.

The British Navy reinforced its defenses in the Mediterranean.

October 3 Italian troops invaded Abyssinia. Mussolini's son-in-law and two sons led the air force to provide cover.

Abyssinia requested protection from the League of Nations.

Italy telegraphed that it was a precautionary measure.

October 4 General de Bono, the Italian High Commissioner in East Africa, declared war.

Page 8

Anglo-French Paris Conference Decides to Continue Cooperation; French Cabinet Approves Economic Sanctions, Awaiting League of Nations Decision for Implementation

(Paris) French Premier Laval and British Cabinet Minister Eden discussed the agenda for the League of Nations Council meeting on Saturday and Sunday at the Foreign Ministry here today. The discussion lasted for one hour and fifteen minutes. Afterwards, a communiqué was issued stating that the British and French officials had studied various procedures to be adopted by the Council meeting. Upon arrival in Geneva, the two sides will continue to cooperate. (Reuters, 3rd)

(Paris) The cabinet held an emergency meeting at 2:30 p.m. today. It is reported that Laval has received almost unanimous support for the League of Nations Council to determine Italy as an aggressor and to decide on economic sanctions against Italy. (Reuters, 4th)

(Paris) According to semi-official sources, Laval and Eden have agreed that sanctions will be purely economic and financial in nature, implemented gradually in stages over a period of time. The timeline for each stage and the focus of gradual implementation will be determined later. It is necessary for the League of Nations to first determine who is the aggressor before considering any sanctions. (Reuters, 3rd)

(Paris) Today's cabinet meeting will approve the Anglo-French cooperation agreement. British Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden and French Premier and Foreign Minister Laval have already reached an agreement on this matter. It is widely believed here today that this important resolution will promote an Anglo-French defensive military alliance. However, the Foreign Ministry denied today that Eden and Laval had already discussed economic sanctions, saying that this matter should be decided by the League of Nations. However, it is understood that the two officials did agree on a plan to quickly contain the African war. The cabinet will therefore decide to assist Britain in enforcing the League Covenant in the League of Nations. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Paris) The government is scheduled to hold a cabinet meeting at 5 p.m. to decide on a policy regarding the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Premier and Foreign Minister Laval will present a report on his discussions with British Minister without Portfolio Eden yesterday afternoon. It is reported that Laval explained the French government's views to Eden yesterday: first, France is prepared to participate in sanctions if the issue can be negotiated and approved internationally; second, France will request that Britain accept mutual obligations, that is, if France takes sanctions against Italy, then in the event of other incidents in Europe, other countries in danger, such as Czechoslovakia, which may be in danger, must be assisted, and it is hoped that Britain will support France at that time; third, France wants to clearly distinguish between collective action and individual action, and hopes that Anglo-French cooperation will not be limited to current acts of aggression, but will also jointly prepare for sanctions against the threat of aggression, so as not to be accused of instigating this act of aggression. In short, Premier Laval emphasizes mutual cooperation between Great Britain and France, including cooperation between the Anglo-French general staffs, in order to prevent the threat of aggression, that is, to enhance the effectiveness of the Locarno Pact. As for accepting mutual obligations, Eden has made some guarantees, but the two sides have not fully agreed on the manner in which sanctions should be implemented against Italy. Laval will explain three points to Eden: (A) French public opinion is divided on the issue of sanctions, and most believe that good understanding should be maintained with both Great Britain and Italy at the same time; (B) Negotiations can still be conducted with Italy before the League of Nations meeting designates the aggressor and before sanctions are implemented; (C) France's final attitude will be decided by the cabinet meeting. Today's cabinet meeting will take into account French public opinion and only consider economic sanctions, starting with severing commercial relations as a means of dealing with Italy. (Havas, 4th)

(Paris) News here today is that France must first establish an Anglo-French air force alliance before allowing Britain to assist it if it is attacked by the Italian or other countries' navies without provocation. British Minister without Portfolio Eden is said to have been ordered to notify France that the current Italo-Abyssinian conflict cannot be used as a pretext to force Britain to conclude this treaty with France against European aggressor countries. Furthermore, according to reliable sources, British officials have begun to study whether to prohibit Italian warships from passing through the Suez Canal, but there is currently no indication of sealing off the canal and prohibiting all ships from passing through. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(London) Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden has returned home to coordinate with the government and has taken the route through Paris to Geneva. Eden has been given secret orders to insist on implementing sanctions against any country that violates the League Covenant. (National Society News Agency, 3rd)

(London) British cabinet members are preparing to convene an emergency cabinet meeting on Saturday and Sunday after the Council meeting in Geneva. If the issue of sanctions is to become a reality, then a special session of Parliament will be convened to pass the plans proposed by the cabinet. (Reuters, 4th)

(Geneva) The Thirteen-Nation Committee met today for two and a half hours and decided to order the previous Five-Nation Committee, which failed to mediate, to investigate "the differences between Italy and Abyssinia" and then report on the strengths and weaknesses of the two countries in this dispute. Abyssinia has reported to the League of Nations that Italian planes bombed the Red Cross hospital near Aduwa, dropping 78 bombs. However, the Thirteen-Nation Committee has decided to notify Abyssinia that, given the change in circumstances, there is no need to send neutral observers as requested by Abyssinia. Italian circles here have all stated that the claim that Italian planes bombed Aduwa is groundless and have verbally denied it to the League of Nations Secretariat. The Thirteen-Nation Committee has dispatched the Five-Nation Committee to revise the historical facts of the dispute in the report drafted by the League of Nations Secretariat. The committee did not discuss the situation caused by today's events, as the Council will meet on Saturday and Sunday to discuss how to deal with this matter. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Paris) After arriving here from Britain, British Minister without Portfolio Eden, accompanied by British Ambassador to France Clerk, visited Premier and Foreign Minister Laval at the Foreign Ministry at 5:50 p.m. At 8 p.m., Laval declared to Havas reporters, "British Minister without Portfolio Eden and I have just discussed the procedures for the League of Nations Council meeting. The Council has now decided to meet on Saturday morning. In addition, the two of us have carefully studied the various procedures contained in the League Covenant. In short, we will continue to cooperate in Geneva." (Havas, 3rd)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council has decided to meet at 10:30 a.m. on Saturday. It is learned here today that Italy is likely to follow in the footsteps of Japan and Germany and withdraw from the League of Nations. The current issue facing the League of Nations is whether member states, under the leadership of Great Britain, are prepared to impose economic or military sanctions on Italy. It is generally believed that moderate economic sanctions are feasible, but there are doubts about military sanctions. It is also learned that the League of Nations has decided to request assistance from the United States to counter Italian aggression. This assistance will include the following points: (1) the United States will send observers to Abyssinia; (2) it will invoke the Neutrality Act, prohibiting the transport of arms to belligerent countries; (3) it will join in economic sanctions, boycotting Italian goods and refusing to sell any goods to Italians. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Geneva) British Minister without Portfolio Eden arrived here this morning from Paris and met with Spanish representative Madariaga, chairman of the Thirteen-Nation Committee on the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, and informed him that the working procedures of the committee had been agreed upon in Paris, that is, the committee would submit a report to the Council, limited to describing the origins of the dispute, and that political issues, especially the issue of sanctions, would be decided by the Council itself. Eden plans to meet with representatives of the member states of the Council in the afternoon. British sources have expressed satisfaction with the discussions between Eden and French Premier Laval yesterday, saying that Great Britain and France have reached complete agreement. (Havas, 4th)

League of Nations Receives Report of Italian Aircraft Bombing; 76 Canisters Dropped on Aduwa

(Geneva) Today, the Secretariat of the League of Nations received a telegram from the Abyssinian Emperor stating that planes had again attacked the town of Aduwa for the second time today, dropping a total of 76 bombs, one of which hit the Red Cross hospital. The League of Nations is once again in a dilemma regarding today's incident, as it must determine whether the act of aggression has already been realized and, if so, who is responsible. If the League of Nations Council makes a judgment based on unverified reports, the impact will be extremely serious. If the act of aggression has been verified, it is expected that the Council will ask the aggressor to withdraw to its original lines and will propose other suggestions for ending the war. This move will require the convening of the League of Nations General Assembly, but it cannot be convened before the end of next week. The Thirteen-Nation Committee met today to discuss the report drafted by the League of Nations Secretariat. Although the League of Nations is proceeding with everything as quickly as possible, today's incident has still caught the League of Nations off guard. The committee now feels that it cannot cope with this new situation, so it has decided to convene a Council meeting on Saturday. The committee has also decided to notify the Abyssinian government that, in view of recent developments, it is no longer necessary to send observers to Abyssinia. Italian circles here all claim that the claim that Italian planes bombed Aduwa is groundless and have verbally denied it to the League of Nations Secretariat. The Thirteen-Nation Committee has sent the Five-Nation Committee to revise the historical facts of the dispute in the report drafted by the League of Nations Secretariat. The committee did not discuss the situation caused by today's incident, as the Council will meet on Saturday and Sunday to discuss how to deal with this matter. (Reuters, 3rd)

(Rome) Military authorities told Associated Press reporters today that the primary objective of the Italian army is to encircle French and British Somaliland in order to prevent arms from being shipped into Abyssinia after the two countries lift the arms embargo. (National News Agency, 4th)

(Geneva) The Italian Embassy here sent a letter to the League of Nations this morning denying that Italian troops had occupied Mausaari or advanced in that direction. At the same time, the Abyssinian government also telegraphed the Secretariat of the League of Nations denying that Abyssinia had taken any action to provoke the Italian invasion. (Reuters, 4th)

The Situation in the Mediterranean

Gibraltar Exercises Air Defense; Six French Submarines Open in the Philippines

Gibraltar Today the local sea and air forces held a joint air defense exercise. All the lights in the city were turned off at night. When the air force carried out a simulated bombing, all the lights on the warships on the harbor surface and the cars on the road were also turned off. (Havas, 4th)

Alexandria After receiving the news that the war in East Africa has broken out, the local authorities immediately ordered the police to gather at important locations, ordered the town to prepare for unexpected changes, and sent military police to station at the submarine cable bureau. All Italian police had surrendered their weapons a week ago (Reuters, 3rd)

Algiers Six French submarines arrived here today, and a large number of warships will probably arrive again, because the Mediterranean has reached a dangerous level (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Paris) British jurists are now studying the issue of prohibiting Italian military vessels from passing through the Suez Canal. There is still doubt as to whether this move is an economic sanction or an act of war. (National News Agency, 3rd)

Athens The Naval Department today telegraphed all Greek ships to avoid passing through the Suez Canal as much as possible. This move is thought to be out of fear that a crisis will occur there, causing "trouble." (National News Agency, 3rd)

US State Department Drafts Arms Embargo Order

To be issued after confirmation of war news

(Washington) The United States is quite concerned about the development of the situation in East Africa, as it may spread to Europe. Today, the State Department held another important meeting, attended by Mr. Moore, Director of the Near East Division, which shows that the State Department has paid attention to the future of the Mediterranean. Secretary of State Hull today also consulted with Undersecretary Phillips, Assistant Secretary Moore, and Mr. Dunn, an expert on African affairs. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull and the State Department have drafted an order declaring a ban on arms exports, which will be submitted to President Roosevelt for approval as soon as the situation in East Africa is officially confirmed. (Reuters, 4th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull said today that the United States must wait for the situation to become clear before implementing an arms embargo on Italy and Abyssinia. Therefore, the US government is unlikely to take any action before receiving an official report confirming that the war has indeed begun. The State Department has not yet received this report, but the government also has its central idea, which is to maintain neutrality. Hull also said that no other country has consulted the United States on its attitude towards implementing sanctions. According to previous news from London, the British Foreign Office was preparing to consult the United States. Observers believe that the United States may cooperate with the League of Nations as much as possible within the scope of its constitution and laws to maintain world peace. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(New York) An anti-fascist riot broke out here today. The authorities urgently summoned 1,250 special police officers to suppress it. Black people in Harlem had clashed with Italian expatriates in New York. School children in Brooklyn were also said to have had similar racial strife. (National News Agency, 3rd)

Japan Strictly Adheres to Neutrality

And hopes that the League of Nations will resolve it peacefully

(Tokyo) The Japanese government telegraphed its ambassadors and ministers to various countries on the morning of the 4th, stating Japan's attitude toward the Italo-Abyssinian War and instructing them to convey it to the governments of the countries they were stationed in. The content roughly stated that the Japanese government would strictly adhere to a neutral attitude toward the Italo-Abyssinian War and hoped that the League of Nations would resolve the war peacefully. (Japanese United News Agency, 4th)

(Tokyo) Today, a spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs refused to criticize the League of Nations' decision to impose sanctions on Italy and could not predict what action Japan would take regarding the League of Nations' future decisions, but said that it was necessary to wait for the situation to become clear. The spokesman replied to questions from reporters, saying that if the Italo-Abyssinian War breaks out, Japan will bear the full responsibility of a neutral country in accordance with international conventions. Japan is not a member of the League of Nations and therefore has no obligations to the League of Nations. The League of Nations must be maintained by the member states of the League of Nations themselves. If the maintenance of the League Covenant depends on the cooperation of non-member states, then the existence of the League of Nations can be said to depend on non-member states. (Reuters, 4th)

Rumors of an October Coup in Japan

The military will demand a thorough investigation of the Mingzheng case; the Okada cabinet will have difficulty remaining in office

(Tokyo) In order to cope with the Second World War that has already broken out, the instigation of right-wing groups, and the internal discord of the Okada Cabinet, the Japanese October coup theory that was temporarily spread in the political circles has once again raised its head. The main reason is that the military, rural veterans' groups, and various right-wing groups have expressed strong opposition to the non-prosecution case of Dr. Mino. It is reported that Minister of the Army Kawashima will represent the military and demand that Prime Minister Okada immediately dismiss Councilor Igi and Director-General of the Legislation Bureau Kanamori and make another statement clarifying the state system. If Okada does not approve, he may resign immediately. It is said that the opinions of the Ministry of the Navy are also becoming more radical. Naval Minister Osumi and fleet officers will also express the same attitude as Minister Kawashima. Therefore, the fate of the current Okada Cabinet is very urgent. Rumors of a coup within this month are therefore rampant. The most promising candidates for the next cabinet are currently Saito, Ugaki, Hiranuma, Konoe, and Minami. However, the Ugaki cabinet theory, which was the most hopeful in the past, has disappeared due to the Nagata incident. The same is true for the Minami cabinet. The Hiranuma and Konoe cabinets seem to be too early. Therefore, it is inferred that Saito is the most likely to succeed as prime minister. If so, the candidates for cabinet members will not be beyond the following situation: (Prime Minister) Saito Makoto, (Home Minister) Yamamoto Tatsuo, (Finance Minister) Takahashi Korekiyo, (Foreign Minister) Hirota Koki, (Agriculture Minister) Goto Fumio, (Commerce Minister) Machida Chuji, (Communications Minister) Yoshida Shigeru, (Railway Minister) sent from the House of Peers, (Education Minister) Horiguchi Yoshijiro, (Colonial Minister) Yamamoto Jotaro, (Justice Minister) Suzuki Kisaburo, the two military ministers will still be re-elected, (Chief Secretary) Karasawa Toshiki. The characteristic of this new cabinet is that it is linked with the Seiyukai to replace the new parties such as Uchida and Yamazaki, or it may welcome Seiyukai President Suzuki to join the cabinet. However, its nature as a bureaucratic, political party, and military bloc regime has not changed. (China Alliance News Agency, 4th)

Japan's Western Mutual Conference; Concrete Policies Toward China

(Tokyo) After the cabinet meeting on the 4th, Prime Minister Okada, Minister of Finance Takahashi, Foreign Minister Hirota, and Minister of the Army Kawashima discussed the fundamental policy toward China, which was previously decided by the Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy. Foreign Minister Hirota first reported that in view of the situation in North China, it was necessary to rebuild the policy toward China, and the process of internally determining the policy toward China was agreed upon by the various ministries. Next, Minister of Finance Takahashi also expressed his opinions. Finally, the ministers discussed various concrete matters, and the meeting was adjourned after an hour. (Japanese United News Agency, 4th)

Situation of Our Citizens Amidst the Italo-Abyssinian Conflict

(Nanjing) Today, someone visited Wang Zhiyuan, Secretary-General of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, and inquired about the recent situation of our citizens in Abyssinia, East Africa, and Italy. According to him, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has already conducted a survey of the number of overseas Chinese in South Africa, but there are no accurate survey reports for the East African region. Although there are records, they may not be accurate. However, the number of overseas Chinese in East Africa is very limited. Although there are more overseas Chinese in Italy, they are currently stable. Unfortunately, the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has finally led to a war, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission will instruct the citizens there to plan for their safety in the vicinity. (Special Dispatch, 4th)

The Impact on Our Country Following the Outbreak of Hostilities Between Italy and Abyssinia

(Nanjing) Foreign dispatches report the outbreak of war between Italy and Abyssinia. As of the fourth of this month, our Ministry of Foreign Affairs had not yet received a telegram from Liu Wendao, our ambassador to Italy. General observation suggests that the Italo-Abyssinian war is not merely a dispute between the two countries, but sufficient to affect world peace. Various international relations will be affected, and the impact on our country's foreign trade will be especially apparent. Economic expert Ma Yinchu said that if the war is limited to Italy and Abyssinia, China can barely hope to maintain its position even amidst the global economic recession. However, if it widens even slightly, China's silk and tea exports will greatly decline or even become completely unsalable, which will have a significant economic impact on China. Regarding the current economic situation in China, the people of the country should work together for stability. Furthermore, Shi Cigu Piyagang said that with the outbreak of the Italo-Abyssinian war, the extent of involvement of European countries will inevitably lead to its impact on the world economy, which is beyond doubt. Our country's foreign trade will inevitably suffer a blow. The Ministry of Industry has been paying attention to this since the occurrence of the Italo-Abyssinian issue and is planning measures to deal with Sino-foreign trade after the outbreak of war. These measures are still in the planning stage. (Fourth day special dispatch)

The Ministry of Finance Strictly Orders the Investigation and Prohibition of Speculators Spreading Rumors

(Nanjing) Recently, the Ministry of Finance noted that a small number of speculators in Shanghai are creating various rumors and wantonly slandering major banks, which foreign newspapers are using without scrutiny. This is disrupting the market and financial order and violating the law. On the fourth of the month, separate letters and telegrams were sent to the military and police authorities in Shanghai, ordering them to rigorously investigate and arrest those spreading rumors and to severely punish them. (Fourth day special dispatch)

Wu Heling Pays Respects to Wang

(Nanjing) Wu Heling paid respects to President Wang at 10:00 AM on the fourth, detailing the recent telegrams from the two princes of Yun and De reporting the recent situation of the West Gong Banner dispute. He also requested that President Wang preside over the resolution of the dispute. Wang instructed Wu to convey the Central Government's concern for Mongolian affairs to all parties when attending the Mongolian Political Council meeting at the temple, hoping to follow the principle of pacifying the people and protecting the tranquility of the border. He also said that the government would dispatch personnel to thoroughly investigate the West Gong Banner dispute soon, aiming to achieve a fair resolution. Furthermore, whether Yu Feipeng will go to Mongolia needs to be determined next week. (Fourth day Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) Wu Heling, head of the Mongolian League and Banner Offices in Nanjing, went to the Executive Yuan at 10:00 AM on the fourth to pay respects to President Wang and reported on the situation of the West Gong Banner. After listening to the report, Wang stated to Wu that our country is currently in a time of crisis, and internal misunderstandings should be eliminated. We should unite as one to strengthen border defense. The Central Government is determined to resolve the West Gong Banner dispute through fair and appropriate measures, so that all parties can accept it. He asked Wu to convey the Central Government's intentions to all parties, asking them to make concessions and not insist on their original positions. Furthermore, Li Hongwen, the representative of the Taiyuan Pacification Headquarters, also reported to President Wang on the fourth. (Fourth day special dispatch)

The Mongolian Political Council's Office in Beiping is Established

(Beiping) The Mongolian Political Council's office in Beiping was established today. Bao Yueqing, the head of the office, reported to the press today on the establishment of the office. Bao said that the two princes, De and Yun, arrived at Bailingmiao on the first of this month and have telegraphed committee members in various places, asking them to attend the meeting before the ninth to participate in the general assembly. He will remain in Beiping, waiting to travel with the committee members. Regarding the West Gong Banner dispute, there is currently no progress. It is said that the Central Government will send Yu Feipeng to the north to mediate, but the Mongolian side has not received this report. (Fourth day special dispatch)

Dispute Over French Road Construction in Wuchuan County

(Nanjing) A person from Wuchuan County, Guangdong, who came to Nanjing, spoke about the dispute over French road construction. The Jin Yu Village and other places in the Sanbai Township of Dong'an Town, Wuchuan County, are all adjacent to Guangzhou Bay (Kwangchow Wan), but are separated by the Honggou River. The area south of the river is a French concession, and the area north of the river belongs to Wuchuan County. Since the demarcation, several decades have passed, and peace has always prevailed. A month ago, the French authorities in Guangzhou Bay suddenly encroached north of the Honggou River from Hongling and built a military road in Sanbai Township. According to the road construction plan, they planned to cross the Honggou River from Hongling, pass through Jin Yu Village, and then turn back to build along the shoreline of the Honggou River. The Wuchuan County Government telegraphed the Provincial Government, requesting instructions on how to respond. The Provincial Government immediately sent a letter to Gan Jiehou, the Foreign Affairs Inspector for Guangdong and Guangxi, to negotiate with the French authorities stationed in Guangdong. At that time, the road from Hongling to Jin Yu Village, about one li in length, had already been built. After Gan's negotiations, the French authorities were able to consider Sino-French relations and immediately stopped the construction of this section of the road. However, after the construction of this section of the road was stopped, they hired hundreds of workers a month ago to build a military road eastward from the beach near the Nine Mothers Temple. However, this beach leads directly to the ocean and is an important waterway for ships to transport goods. Now that the French are blocking the beach to build a road, it will greatly affect the future transportation of ships and the livelihoods of the people. Gan is currently negotiating with the French authorities, and a resolution should be reached soon. (Fourth day special dispatch)

The Shantou Case is Expected to be Resolved Locally

(Nanjing) The Shantou rice tax dispute has been resolved locally through negotiations between Gan Jiehou, the Shantou Municipal Government, and the Japanese side, and there is generally no problem. A certain committee member from Guangdong received a private telegram from Guangzhou yesterday stating that the Guangdong Provincial Government has not paid enough attention to this matter. After the Japanese Consul-General stationed in Guangzhou raised the issue with the authorities, the authorities replied that this matter falls within the scope of local negotiations and agreed to handle it locally. They also, at the request of the Japanese side, specially instructed the inspector's office and the Shantou Municipal Government to handle the matter carefully and maintain good relations between the two countries. Foreign dispatches have exaggerated the matter. Furthermore, according to information from our diplomatic circles, the Japanese Embassy has never formally raised this matter with our Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Li Hanun was ordered by the Provincial Government to telegraph the province for instructions on how to handle the Japanese merchants' smuggled goods seized in Shantou, handling it with caution. On the third, a batch of rice was first shipped by Japanese merchants to the province, who refused to pay the special agricultural product tax and directly transported it to warehouses in Shamian. The Department of Finance reported to the headquarters and requested instructions from the Provincial Government. Since the previous month, Japanese merchants have often imported other kinds of goods, refusing to pay the special tax. The Agricultural Tax Bureau seized a batch of Japanese paper, which was subsequently returned after negotiations by the Japanese consul. The Agricultural Tax Bureau's monthly revenue was 1.5 to 1.6 million. Since the Japanese began smuggling goods, it has sharply decreased, falling to 900,000 last month. (Fourth day dispatch)

The Legislative Yuan Discusses Various Railway Regulations

The Law on Appeals and Other Cases Are Amended and Passed

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 31st meeting of the Agricultural Committee on the fourth. Seventy-three committee members, including Lian Shenghai, attended, with Sun Ke presiding and Liang Hancao as Secretary-General. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) Amendment of Article 9, Clause 7, and Article 16 of the Organizational Law of the Ministry of the Navy, resolved and passed. (2) Amendment of the Private Railway Regulations. (3) Amendment of the Special Railway Regulations. (4) Review of the Local Government-Operated Railway Regulations. Regarding the above three cases, due to issues such as the use of foreign capital and the issuance of company bonds by companies, the committee members had heated debates, and all agreed that representatives from the responsible departments should be invited to conduct more thorough research. Therefore, it was unanimously resolved to refer the cases back to a committee of seven members, including Ma Yinchu, Lian Shenghai, Zheng Hongnian, Wei Tingsheng, Chen Changheng, Shi Shangkuan, and Chen Guyuan, to be convened by Ma Yinchu. (5) The Civil Service Office requested an interpretation of whether appeals, further appeals, or direct administrative lawsuits could be filed against decisions made by government-administered agencies. It was resolved to amend and pass the Law on Appeals according to the results of the review by the Legal System Committee. (6) Amendment of the Administrative Litigation Law, resolved and passed. (7) Amendment of Article 1 of the Administrative Litigation Fee Regulations, resolved and passed. The amended article is as follows: The administrative litigation forms shall be manufactured and promulgated by the Judicial Yuan, and fees shall be collected according to the following regulations: 1. Litigation form: 5 jiao. 2. Attorney's authorization letter: 5 jiao. (Fourth day Central News Agency dispatch)

Chairman Lin's Statement Regarding Lin Jing

(Nanjing) Chairman Lin issued a statement to reporters on the fourth regarding Lin Jing, saying that Lin Jing is his nephew, and he has always treated him as a nephew. There has been no inheritance procedure, and he has never been regarded as an adopted son. Legally, there are no issues. Moreover, he is already an adult, and in fact, there is no way to effectively interfere with or consider his personal actions. In the future, he will absolutely not be responsible for all his actions legally or in fact. (Fourth day Central News Agency dispatch)

Zhang Yuanfu Talks About the Inaccuracy of Xinjiang's Communist Affiliation

(Tianjin) Zhang Yuanfu, the representative of Xinjiang stationed in Tianjin, stated that communication between Dihua and the Tianjin office has been constant, and his personal friendship with Governor Sheng is strong. If there were any matters such as alliance with Russia or communist affiliation, he would never conceal them from him. Foreign newspapers continue to use their old tricks of fabricating rumors, which are not worth refuting. However, many people in the country are not clear about the situation in Xinjiang, so it is necessary to clarify. Xinjiang has complex ethnicities, and many people believe in religion. In this regard, it is impossible to tolerate communism, let alone Governor Sheng. Even if he had this intention, the various ethnic groups would never agree. Recently, the Xinjiang Industrial and Commercial Bank, telegraph offices, schools, and rural cooperatives have been successively established, with everything that central banks should have. More than 150 schools have been established, and recently, more than 100 teachers and civil servants who resigned have been hired from Beiping and are waiting to be transported by train. These talents do not have communist ideology or theories, and Xinjiang's hiring of them proves that the rumors of communist affiliation are inaccurate. (Fourth day special dispatch)

The Ministry of Industry Pays Attention to Foreign Exchange

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry believes that in recent years, many countries' governments have devalued their currencies and managed exchange rates to increase exports. Actions such as the United States' increase in the price of silver, Britain, Belgium, and Japan abandoning the gold standard, and Germany's control of exchange rates have severely impacted our country's foreign trade. Furthermore, our country's foreign exchange is manipulated by foreign banks. The Ministry of Industry is working to guide merchants to strengthen ties and urge our country's banks to carry out financial adjustments and assistance for import and export trade. (Fourth day special dispatch)

Large Groups of Bandits Rampage Near the Liujiang River

(Beiping) A telegram from Qinhuangdao states that there have been many lurking bandits in various places near the Liujiang River in recent days. Large groups of bandits have disintegrated into smaller units, robbing and kidnapping everywhere. Small groups of bandits have also been found in Funing, Shimen, Haiyangzhen, and other places in recent days. The war zone authorities have issued orders to all public security bureaus to tighten the encirclement and suppression efforts. The Yellow River Water Has Passed Shuyang and Mostly Flows Towards Dongguan

The Dykes of Both Counties Are Under Strain, the Fanhe Dyke in Yaowan Has Collapsed, and the Three Counties Are Cooperatively Defending the Chaimi Dyke

(Qingjiangpu) The crest of the Yellow River flood has passed Liuyang and is mostly flowing directly towards Dongguan and Guanyun counties. The lower reaches of Wanggong in Donghai County are under strain, and the area near Longgou in Guanyun County is under strain. All sailing ships entering the area have been detained. The amount of salt in Xiba has decreased rather than increased. According to those returning from the sea, many people in the sea area are hiring boats to prepare for escape, and ships are in great demand. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Qingjiangpu) According to information from the flood control office in the canal area, the southern dyke of the Fanhe River in Yaowan collapsed for more than twenty zhang on the morning of the fourth. The floodwaters flowed directly towards Luoma Lake, and the water level at the bamboo basket dam dropped sharply by eight cun that day. County Magistrate Su Zhang reported to the office that the losses were very heavy. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Zhenjiang) The water from Weishan Lake is rushing into Huangdun Lake, and there are four breaches in the western dyke of Yaowan, making the situation extremely urgent. The water level at Wuhua Bridge has risen by one chi, and the lower reaches of Suqian and Liutang are in danger. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Xuzhou) In addition to ordering Hao Commissioner of the Donghai area to be responsible for presiding over flood control in the three counties, the Jiangsu Provincial Government recently ordered the county magistrates of Donghai, Guanyun, and Shuyang to do their best to protect the flood control of the Yishu River according to plan, fulfilling their responsibilities. They should not have any conflicts or arbitrarily divide their areas, causing disturbances to each other. They should wholeheartedly fight against the flood, unite in spirit, and not have the mentality of benefiting oneself at the expense of one's neighbors, aiming to guide the water into the sea. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The Drainage and Conservancy Office recently ordered the county magistrates of Donghai, Guanyun, and Shuyang to, one, according to reports, after the breach of Liutang, the three counties of Donghai, Guanyun, and Shuyang should jointly defend the north bank of the Chaimi Dyke. Guanyun County should abandon the north bank of the Chaimi Dyke and retreat to the east bank of the Yanhe River to seek local safety. If the three counties can cooperatively defend the north bank of the Chaimi Dyke, the situation is still manageable. Although the disaster area is large, it should not harm the salt area. They should still jointly defend it to ensure safety. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Qingjiangpu) According to a telegram from Shuyang, the town of Tanggou in the county is surrounded by water, and the residents are trapped in the water. In addition, there are disaster victims fleeing from Qianwei and other places in the past, and the price of firewood and rice has soared. Moreover, since the county was hit by the Yellow River flood, the southeastern half of the county has been flooded, and boats can travel everywhere. Farmers in the disaster area are now selling their plowing cattle, with each head costing at most 10 yuan. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Jinan) Zhang Honglie's letter to Qin Fen: (1) Shandong has exhausted its funds for dyke closure and cannot bear the burden. (2) If only 20% of the dyke closure funds are allocated before construction begins, the materials cannot be purchased completely, delaying the project. The current situation at the decided location is slightly better, with two-thirds of the floodwaters flowing into the area and the remainder returning to the main river. Now, eight-tenths of the floodwaters are flowing into the area, and only two-tenths are flowing into the main river. The breach is still 700 meters wide. The Lishuntun residual embankment is collapsing in the north and silting up in the south, which is not of great importance. (Fourth day special dispatch)

(Fourth day Central News Agency dispatch)

The Process of Amending the Law on Appeals

(Nanjing) The Civil Service Office of the National Government previously received appeals from the Min'an Co., Ltd. due to dissatisfaction with the decision of the Training Directorate regarding the case of long-term occupancy of houses, and from Wang Dunxu Hall in Wuxi due to dissatisfaction with the decision of the Executive Yuan regarding the case of land disputes. They filed further appeals to the Civil Service Office of the National Government one after another. The office considered that the issue of jurisdiction over further appeals filed by agencies directly under the National Government was still doubtful under the current system. After signing its opinions, it was submitted to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation. The Judicial Yuan replied that there were no relevant provisions in the current laws and regulations that could be used for interpretation. Therefore, it was again submitted to the Central Political Council for review. After the review by the Legal System Group of the Central Political Council, the following principles were supplemented: Anyone who is dissatisfied with the decisions or dispositions of agencies not directly under the National Government of the Five Yuan does not need to go through the further appeal procedure and may directly file an administrative lawsuit. The Secretariat of the Central Political Council further added that this supplemented principle of the Legal System Group is in line with actual needs, but there are still two doubts: (1) When filing an appeal against a decision or disposition of the Five Yuan and agencies directly under the National Government, which should be the accepting agency? (2) According to the current laws and regulations, people can only file an administrative lawsuit against a decision on further appeal if the original decision is illegal. This decision of the Legal System Group seems to allow the filing of administrative lawsuits regardless of whether the decision is illegal or inappropriate, and the boundary seems unclear. When this review report of the Legal System Group was submitted to the Central Political Council, Minister of Justice Wang Yongbin also advocated deleting the last sentence of the principles of the Legal System Group, "may directly file an administrative lawsuit." The Central Political Council then decided to submit the letter from the Civil Service Office of the National Government, the review opinions of the Legal System Group, Wang Yongbin's opinions, and the Secretariat's annotations to the Legislative Yuan for review. After the review by the Legislative Yuan on the fourth, the Law on Appeals was amended to allow those who are dissatisfied with the decisions of the Five Yuan or other agencies directly under the National Government to file an appeal with the original agency. At the same time, the Administrative Litigation Law was also amended to allow those who are dissatisfied with a decision made in accordance with the Law on Appeals after filing an appeal or further appeal against an illegal disposition to file an administrative lawsuit. (Fourth day Central News Agency dispatch)

Zhongda Initiates the Organization of the Chinese Mental Hygiene Association

(Nanjing) Professors from the College of Education of Zhongda University plan to initiate the organization of the Chinese Mental Hygiene Association and have sent letters to leaders from all walks of life to solicit initiators. U.S. Warships Gather for Exercises at Qinhuangdao

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 2nd, the U.S. transport ship USS Chaumont, commanded by Captain Dremen, arrived at Qinhuangdao with 38 officers and 420 soldiers. On the same evening, the communication ship USS Pigeon, commanded by Captain Orita, also sailed from Qingdao with 61 officers and soldiers. Both were docked at the Kailuan No. 2 pier. Recently, more and more Japanese residents along the Beining Railway line have moved in. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Red Army Appears Along the Yalu River

(Tianjin) According to a dispatch from Shenyang, the Red area along the Yalu River is expanding. The army commanded by a certain Commander Yang of the Red Army has more than 1,000 people. Three people, including Guhe Group Japanese employees Kiki Tatsuo and Kiki Miichi, as well as a Korean truck driver, were taken away by the Red Army in Ji'an Red Area on September 29. The next day, the garrison stationed in the eastern border region engaged the Red Army near Datunzigou in the eighth district of Ji'an. Dozens of soldiers were killed and more than ten were wounded. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Yin Tong Does Not Participate in Foreign-Related Matters

(Tianjin) Yin Tong issued a statement saying that in recent years, his involvement in foreign-related matters in the north was under the order of the chairman of the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee, and he acted as a consultant to mediate. After the end of the Political Readjustment Committee, this position was also automatically removed. Except for railway affairs, he does not participate in any foreign-related matters. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Wei Shuhong Appointed Chief of Staff of Hebei Security Department

(Baoding) After the reorganization of the Hebei Security Office, Shang Zhen has now announced the appointment of Wei Shuhong as Chief of Staff of the Security Command and Li Xingcun as Director of the Security Office. From now on, official documents to the outside will be issued in the name of the Security Command. (4th, Central News Agency)

(Guihua) Wang Jingguo arrived in Wuyuan from Baotou on the 3rd to inspect the reclamation situation. He has scheduled a defense meeting to be held on the 5th, bringing together military and political organs, and local gentry from Wuyuan, Linhe and Anbei counties. He will also explore and arrange the defense of western Suiyuan in the vicinity. (4th, Central News Agency)

Huaianing Provincial Government decided at its regular meeting on the 4th to appoint Zhang Jie as the chief of the Linhuai Public Security Bureau. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Guiyang) The Construction Department received a telegram from the Eastern Route Engineering Office stating that the Hunan-Guizhou Highway has been fully completed. The office was closed on September 30, requesting the dispatch of personnel for acceptance inspection and to send vehicles for trial runs. (4th, Central Dispatch)

Satisfactory Negotiations for the Return of the Chenqi to the Fleet

(Qingdao) Xie Gangzhe returned to Qingdao on the morning of the 2nd. According to his statement to reporters, the matter of the Chenqi and Zhahe returning to the fleet has been negotiated satisfactorily. The two ships are currently temporarily docked in the Yangtze River and will eventually be returned to Qingdao. The monthly expenses required are 50,000 yuan, which will be allocated by the Beiping Military Affairs Commission. More than 100 officers and soldiers of the Zhahe ship have been discharged and settled in the Third Fleet. It is not yet decided when he will return to Weihai. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Commander Hyakutake Arrives in Qingdao from Tianjin

(Qingdao) Lieutenant General Hyakutake, commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, arrived in Qingdao from Tianjin on the warship Mamoshi at 1:00 PM on the 4th, staying for five days. He is scheduled to take the original ship to Shanghai on the 8th. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Kaifeng) A long-distance bus accident occurred on the Bian-Huai line on the 3rd in Fuji North, Qixian County, resulting in one passenger dead and more than ten with broken legs and shoulders. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Drought Disaster in Huangchuan and Gushi

(Kaifeng) Due to drought in Huangchuan and Gushi, the autumn harvest is only 10-20%. Thieves are rampant, and over two hundred people have been burned to death as hostages. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Lifting of Blockades in Various Counties of Jiangxi

(Nanchang) With banditry largely pacified in various counties of Jiangxi, the Civil Affairs Department has convened the Finance, Construction, and Agricultural Cooperative Associations to discuss lifting the blockade of various counties, forming agricultural cooperative branches, taking over the public sales of oil and salt, and implementing controls. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Nanchang) With the military at rest, various departments of the Jiangxi Pacification Headquarters are preparing to close down. The headquarters was established ten months ago and commanded six pacification zones. The work of clearing out remnants of bandits has been completed. Internal staff may be transferred to the Sichuan Field Headquarters. (4th, Central News Agency)

(Hankou) The Field Headquarters has ordered the Provincial Government to provide relief to rural areas in flood-stricken counties according to the methods used in bandit-affected counties. Upon allocation of the Provincial Agricultural Revitalization funds, relief societies will be formed according to relief regulations to provide loans so that disaster victims can restore production as soon as possible. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) The Provincial Government has increased the capital of the Provincial Bank by one million to expand its business and develop the local economy by establishing savings and loan departments and offices throughout the province to complete the provincial financial system. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Xiamen) Lin Shaonan, the Fujian-Zhejiang Foreign Affairs Inspector, took the Yushun ship on the 3rd via Fuzhou, originally bound for Shanghai and then Beijing. He said that the opinions exchanged with the British consulate regarding the Taikoo Wharf flying bridge case were quite similar, and the central government has drafted a solution. This trip will review the inspection report, and then after deliberation, it will be resolved locally, based on the principle of respecting sovereignty and protecting territory. The case of Japanese residents purchasing land in Mao Hou is easy to solve and does not require negotiation. The villagers of Mao Hou are raising funds from Southeast Asia. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Fujian Provincial Miscellaneous Tax on Superstitious Items Allocated to Security Team Expenses

(Fuzhou) The Provincial Government has decided to implement a special tax on superstitious items, with the tax rate set at 30%. It is limited to four items: candles, firecrackers, incense, and foil. It is estimated that the annual revenue will be around 1.2 million. The monthly cost of the security teams is fixed at 220,000, and the entire amount will be allocated from this tax. All kinds of donations levied by the teams locally will be abolished to reduce the burden on the people. (4th, Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The long-distance telephone line operated by the Ministry of Communications for nine provinces has been completed for the Beijing-Xuzhou section. Westbound Observations

— Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Ji Yuan

On the Way to Hankou

On the evening of September 19, this reporter and Mr. Song Hua took the Minsheng Company's Minyang ship for a tour of Sichuan. At about 1:00 AM on the 20th, we drove past Zhenjiang in the lights of the night. On the morning of the 21st, we passed Wuhu. Along the way, the wind was gentle and the sun was bright, and the smoke waves were vast. The disaster scenes of the rain-soaked coast were still vivid. When passing Anqing, it was already twilight, and the evening wind invaded the skin, with a slight chill of late autumn. The afterglow of the setting sun shone on the river, forming a golden color. From time to time, three or four foreign warships and foreign merchant ships drove downwind. The machines and flags fluttered in the dim light, making them even more majestic. At about 5:00 PM on the 12th, the ship arrived in Hankou and berthed at the North German Second Wharf. Because we had to stay in Hankou for several days, we packed our luggage and disembarked.

Impressions After Arriving in Wuhan

Wuhan is a place this reporter has visited before. At that time, before the great flood of the 20th year [of the Republic], the deep impressions left in my mind were "four mores." First, there were more slogans, dazzling and diverse. Second, there were more leather belts, majestic and awe-inspiring. Taking rickshaws would not cost money. Third, there were more killings. From Zhongshan Road to Liubao Bridge, one could see announcements of executions almost every day. Fourth, there were more opium dens and prostitutes, standing everywhere, doing all kinds of evil. This time, revisiting the old place, I feel that the situation has changed somewhat. Although the dazzling slogans can still be seen everywhere, they all seem to be the symbols of the New Life Movement. The slogans of the New Life Movement, "Observe etiquette, know righteousness, be honest, be responsible, and abide by discipline," are the most fashionable slogans. "Simple, plain, realistic, and rapid" are the creeds of the New Life Movement. But unfortunately, these slogans cannot achieve any great effect. In recent days, the Wuhan authorities have been racking their brains over the diplomatic disputes over the slogans. This shows that slogans cannot be posted casually as before.

The majesty of the leather belts has indeed decreased somewhat compared to before, but the majesty of the police has replaced the majesty of the leather belts. According to the survey, incidents of execution seem to be less common. These can be said to be relatively progressive phenomena.

Since the implementation of the New Life Movement, the opium dens and prostitutes in Hankou seem to have decreased on the surface. The situation of selling opium pipes along the street and opening opium dens everywhere is not easily seen after strict crackdowns. However, those familiar with the situation can still list them without omission. It is said that the current anti-smoking policy of the authorities focuses on integrating prohibition into taxation. The annual tax revenue can reach about 10 million yuan, with the aim of completely eliminating it within a few years. Since the ban on prostitution, the prostitutes have moved to the French Concession. The French Concession authorities levy heavy prostitute taxes on prostitutes, increasing a very large income. There are many newly established hotels in the French Concession, and business is still not bad. On the other hand, large and small hotels in the Chinese Concession are all deserted.

In addition, there is a special phenomenon that has occurred in recent years, which is the low cost of labor. Taking rickshaw fares as an example, comparing the rickshaws in the three towns of Wuhan with the rickshaws in Shanghai, the former are several times cheaper than the latter. Often, a journey of four or five li only costs four or five cents, and the rickshaw drivers are still fighting over it. (On average, excluding rent, they can earn about 20 cents a day.) When this reporter first disembarked, the rickshaw drivers were fighting over a one-cent business, and three or five of them almost fought each other, resulting in blood stains on the reporter's hands. If we look at them, their emaciated appearance makes us feel infinite sympathy. As for the general unemployed elderly, weak, and women, their lives are even more miserable.

Shandong Coal Merchants Plead for Relief

Submitting to the Qingdao Municipal Government for Forwarding to the Ministry of Industry, Requesting the Central Government to Allocate Coal Industry Loans

Qingdao Correspondence: Eight companies, including Tongxing Coal Mine in Boshan and other places in eastern Shandong, are facing difficulties in sustaining their business due to the sharp drop in coal prices and lack of capital turnover. They have submitted a request to the Qingdao Municipal Government for forwarding to the Ministry of Industry for assistance, but no results have been obtained. Now that the merchants have heard that the Ministry of Industry is launching loans to assist the coal industry, they have united with their counterparts and submitted another request to the Municipal Government, requesting it to forward the loan request to the Ministry of Industry for assistance. The Municipal Government, upon receiving the request, has forwarded it to the Ministry of Industry to express their sincere plea. The merchants stated in their document to the Municipal Government: "It is found that the Boshan coal mine in eastern Shandong has abundant reserves and excellent quality. According to statistics, the annual output is no less than 2 million tons, and it is transported and sold to provinces both inside and outside the province. The sales volume in places such as Shanghai, Guangdong, Fujian, and Hankou almost exceeds that of our own province. However, since the January 28th Incident, the Shanghai market has been affected by the war, financial stagnation, and commercial depression. Coupled with the dumping of foreign coal, market prices have plummeted. It is even more difficult for domestic coal to maintain its business due to the lack of capital turnover. If the government does not provide assistance in the long run, it is feared that it will be inevitable that they will go bankrupt one after another. In the past, your government sympathized with the hardships of the merchants and advocated the distribution of production and joint sales to provide assistance, which was a good method and intention, and we are deeply grateful. However, as things went against expectations, it has not been realized so far, which has failed the government's intention to maintain industry. Recently, we have heard that the Ministry of Industry is carrying out loans to assist the national coal industry in order to re-lend and assist. The merchants are suffering from a lack of funds and are in a dilemma. Upon hearing the news, they all feel that there is a glimmer of hope for the future. After joint consultation, Zhuang Shuting and Sun Liangchen were recommended to represent them in petitioning the central government to allocate this loan in order to maintain their business. It is reasonable to present this request, requesting you to examine the situation below and approve the transfer to the Ministry of Industry to establish this loan and immediately provide loan assistance to maintain domestic coal and alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. It is a matter of public convenience. Respectfully submitted, Zhuang Shuting, Manager of Tongxing Coal Mine, Zhu Yaoru, Manager of Shandong Coal Mine, Sun Liangchen, Manager of Fuxing Coal Mine, Wang Yucun, Manager of Yide Coal Mine, Li Xingjie, Manager of Lihe Coal Mine, Meng Jingzhou, Manager of Daxing Coal Mine, Cheng Shaolu, Manager of Zhenye Coal Mine, and Cheng Shaolu, Manager of Luxing Coal Mine."

International Commercial Telegraph

— October 4th, Reuters Exclusive Business Intelligence Telegraph —

Gold and Silver

London gold price today is one hundred and forty-one shillings eleven pence and a half, up one penny.

London silver market sales were not high, India and speculators both bought in, causing spot prices to rise by one two five, to twenty-nine pence five six two five, futures rose one eight seven five, to twenty-nine pence six eight seven five.

Exchange Rates

The London foreign exchange market saw very little trading this morning. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was four yuan, eight jiao, nine fen, eight one two five, which was lower than yesterday's closing rate by zero six two five. At one o'clock in the afternoon, it fell another one two five, and at two o'clock it continued to fall two five, to four yuan, eight jiao, nine fen, four three seven five.

The opening exchange rate between the British and French currencies fell five pounds, to seventy-four francs and forty-one cents. At two o'clock in the afternoon, it continued to fall six cents, to seventy-four francs and five cents.

Cotton and Wheat

New York cotton market, spot demand is good, so opening prices rose by seven pounds. Overseas buying appetite is quite strong, resulting in prices continuing to be firm, and then continue to rise, but slightly encounter selling.

Liverpool cotton market, at one o'clock in the afternoon, the price for the January period was 6.11, down four pounds. The English wheat Liverpool wheat market, due to more relaxed Argentine telegrams, there was a downward trend this morning, but there were many purchases later, and prices turned firm. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the price for the November period was six shillings and six and a half pence, down two pence.

Chicago wheat market, due to the decline in the Liverpool and Argentine wheat markets, the opening price fell by half a pound. Later, there were large sales, causing prices to continue to fall. The trend of miscellaneous grains fell with the wheat market, and the opening price was reduced by six one point five.

Rubber

London rubber market was stable this morning, with the transaction price for the January and March periods being six pence, higher than the closing price by one two five. At noon, it fell zero six two five, but the market situation is still stable.

New York rubber rose sixteen pounds due to the firm situation in the London market, but later the market situation turned sluggish due to merchants' unwillingness to trade.

Securities

The New York securities market was firm at the opening this morning, and the prices of various securities rose. Mining and copper stocks rose more significantly. About half an hour later, the market experienced profit-taking. After the profit-taking subsided, prices continued to rise. The average price of the Dow Jones twenty industrial stocks opened up forty-eight cents, to one two nine point five three. The various prices are as follows:
