Southern Journey Impressions

— Special Correspondent Qian Hua of this Newspaper

(43) The Return Journey

Going down the Tan River from Guilin to Yangshuo, the scenery along the way is breathtaking and inexhaustible. Therefore, those who have traveled to Guilin say, "Boating to see the mountains is better than traveling on land." The reception committee also followed this principle, gathering more than seventy large horse-gate boats specifically for members to ride. They departed in batches from the waterway back to Wuzhou. Because it was flood season, the entire journey of 670 li was expected to take three days. If it were after September or October, when the water is shallow and dried up, it would take more than ten days. The reporter was in the last batch, boarding the boat at 10 p.m. on the 21st. The boat was docked beside a pontoon bridge, lined up with more than twenty others. Each boat had a host, carrying six or seven or three or four members, transporting luggage, saying farewell. The scene was extremely lively, and the water was as smooth as a mirror. With a gentle evening breeze, I sat on the bow of the boat, gazing at the shadows of the mountains, feeling broad-minded and free from worries. A nearby boat hired a Guilin folk singer, who played and sang by himself. The melody was like Suzhou Tan Huang, more than half of which I could understand. The crowd on the bridge gradually gathered, and the singer sang even more vigorously, making a disturbance until midnight before leaving. The reporter traveled by car on land for six days, driving for seven or eight hours each day, deeply feeling the hardship of traveling by car. Once switching from car to boat, I felt even more comfortable. The horse-gate boat was extremely spacious, with a cabin that could accommodate more than ten people. In the late Qing dynasty, these boats were originally for civil service examination candidates, so the boat ladies' cooking was particularly exquisite. The boatmen's entire families were engaged in labor, taking on the duties of boat owner, helmsman, cook, rower, and handyman. The order was well-maintained. A small boat was tied alongside, providing a place for the women, children, and girls to sleep. The arrangement was relatively clean, resembling a small room. At dawn on the 23rd, the creaking sound of the oars awakened me from a sweet dream. I got up to see that the boat had already set off, the evening scenery infinitely beautiful. Before long, we arrived at the foot of Elephant Trunk Hill. Looking afar at Rooster Fighting Hill, it truly resembled the image. Along the way, the water flowed rapidly, the cliffs and ravines were secluded and strange, sometimes standing upright in front of us, sometimes jade pillars stretched across the sky. The river course was winding, and the mountains turned with the water, like watching a scenic film, constantly changing. "Guilin's scenery is the best in the world," I now believed without doubt. The twenty-odd good boats chased after each other. On the bows of the boats, all that could be seen were dozens of camera boxes, busily working, which was quite interesting. The boatmen pointed out and explained as we traveled, "This is such-and-such mountain, with such-and-such historical sites; this is such-and-such place, with such-and-such scenic spots." After about three hours of travel, we suddenly saw a steep cliff facing us, the mountain shaped like a pen rack, with green, white, and red colors mixed together, mottled and colorful. The boatman said, "This is Painting Mountain." Faintly visible were several horses, equipped with bridles, some looking up, some looking down, extremely lifelike. Some blessed people could see as many as nine horses. Travelers often use this to predict their fortune. My companions said they saw two horses or four horses. I, the reporter, with my nearsightedness, saw a blurry mess, not a single horse visible. At 6 p.m., we finally arrived at Yangshuo, all boats tied up to the shore at dusk. The members disembarked one after another to visit. The streets and markets of Yangshuo County were extremely narrow, and there were no major merchants or wealthy families, so the situation was unusually desolate. For such a famous scenic area, the scene was like this, probably because transportation was blocked, and tourists just took a quick look and left, not even pausing slightly, thus causing it to become increasingly deserted. The members toured around for a week, and suddenly the evening clouds gathered, making it dark and difficult to distinguish faces. They hurried back to the boats in a panic. The roads were rugged and there were no lights. Fortunately, there were many people, and they took precautions against each other, safely crossing over and boarding the boats. Many people from Guangdong and Guangxi are accustomed to swimming, so because the water was shallow, they lit candles on the bow of the boat. Many members went into the water for a night swim, laughing and talking, full of interest. At dawn the next morning, the boat set sail downstream from Yangshuo. Because the river water gradually became shallow and there were many sandy beaches, the journey was slow. Moreover, from Yangshuo downstream, the scenery gradually became mediocre. The people's boats relied on manpower to navigate, and it gradually became annoying. We arrived at Pingle at noon. Pingle is a prosperous county, and because it is near the West River, everything has the atmosphere of a riverside town. The streets and markets were crowded. The members together went to Zhongshan Park for a short rest. The park used natural scenery as its backdrop, with lush trees, and had a unique charm. On this day, a motorboat going to Wuzhou was parked in the heart of the river. Because of time constraints, the reporter switched to the motorboat, which set sail at 3 p.m. on the 23rd and arrived in Wuzhou at 2 p.m. on the 24th. Military police boarded the boats and ships to search, overturning boxes and bags, extremely strict. The biggest purpose was to find opium. Guangxi relies heavily on opium transit taxes, so it had to strictly prevent smuggling. After staying in Wuzhou for one night, at 1 p.m. on the 25th, I boarded a Hong Kong-Wuzhou boat to Sanshui. Li Zongren's wife, Ms. Guo Dejie, also took the same boat to Guangdong. At 12 p.m. that night, the boat arrived in Sanshui, docked in the heart of the river. Small sampan women came to solicit customers, the situation was fierce. Fortunately, representatives from the Guangdong Provincial Association came to welcome us with large lanterns and prepared ferry boats to transport luggage, allowing us to safely overcome the difficult situation and reach the other shore. We walked about a mile from the ferry to the Guangzhou-1 railway station. The train was to depart at 6 a.m. The train was stuffy and hot, so we all walked on the platform to cool off. Nearby small food stalls, with red lanterns, welcomed guests, preparing chicken and duck congee, wontons, etc., business was booming, resembling the scene of a roadside inn in the north. The night felt long, and after a long time, the sky began to brighten slightly. Madame Li, accompanied only by two adjutants and a maid, with extremely simple luggage, also mingled with the members, waiting bitterly for half the night, without the slightest air of a noble lady, her frugality was admirable. The train departed at six o'clock and arrived at Shiwetang at eleven o'clock. There was a special boat waiting to welcome us, ferrying us to Guangzhou. The scorching heat of Guangzhou had not diminished, the temperature reaching around 100 degrees. It was even worse in the evening. The reporter and a friend took a stroll through the streets, purchasing local goods. At 4 p.m., I took a Hong Kong-Guangdong boat to Hong Kong. When I came, I took the Kowloon-Canton Railway, but this time I returned to Hong Kong by water, enjoying the scenery of Humen. Both the land and water scenery were excellent, it could not be said that my eyes were not blessed. The boat was owned by a British merchant, extremely clean and comfortable. The boat set sail at 4 p.m. I leaned on the railing, looking at the scenery of the Pearl River. At about 5 p.m., we passed Huangpu. From a distance, the white rooftops of the Huangpu Military Academy stood tall in the clouds, disappearing in an instant. At 6:30 p.m., we passed the Humen Fort. The terrain was indeed extremely dangerous. Leaving the Humen estuary, the setting sun was already setting, the remaining glow not yet faded, the distance appearing red, reflected in the sea appearing purple. The winding mountains were like a complete picture. The fishing boats were faint. The Humen sunset was one of the Eight Scenic Spots of Yangcheng, truly not an exaggeration. At 10 p.m., the boat arrived in Hong Kong, and I changed to the Tai Tung Hotel, because there were Shanghai servants. On the evening of the 27th, I boarded the Lincoln President of the Da Lai Company to return to Shanghai. We set sail at 6 a.m. on the 28th. The Chairman of Zhejiang Province, Huang Shaoxiong, and his family were also on the same boat. Huang was from Rong County, Guangxi, and was a classmate and close fellow townsman of Ye Qi. This time, Ye Qi was buried, and he came to hold the ropes. On the way, the Chairman and I discussed the construction and economic problems of Guangxi Province. Huang advocated that each province should develop its own resources with a spirit of self-reliance. Guangxi's tungsten and tin mines had great prospects. The central government was also economically strained. Rumors of subsidies for Guangxi were not true, he said. The boat arrived in Shanghai at 2 p.m. on the 30th. The southern journey was exactly one month long. (The End)

The boat I took on my return journey

The scenery along the Li River from Guilin to Yangshuo

The Li River

Reorganization of Security Forces in the Hebei War Zone

Li Fengyun, Zhao Dian, etc. relieved of duties, Liu Le, etc. causes a commotion

Tianjin Dispatch. In the past week, Yin Rugeng has been traveling busily between Pingjin, repeatedly meeting with Takeashita Yoshiharu, chief of the Kwantung Army's special service agency in Shanhaiguan; Sakai Takashi, chief of staff of the North China garrison army; Takahashi Tan, military attaché at the Japanese embassy in Ping; and others, to discuss the reorganization of the security forces in the war zone. The reorganization planned by our side is for the 3rd Security Brigade under Li Fengyun, the 4th Brigade under Zhao Lei, and the 5th Brigade under Feng Shoupeng and Luo Dongshu, which are awaiting integration. The methods for reorganizing the Li, Luo, and Feng units have been agreed upon and are being implemented in order. Only the Zhao unit has not yet been finalized. Yin specially came to Tianjin on the 1st to meet with Takeashita from Beidaihe to discuss again. It is heard that the most important issue in reorganizing the Zhao unit, such as the size of the force conforming to provincial regulations, a brigade commanding four battalions, with the number of officers and soldiers not exceeding two thousand, is still in discussion. At present, the Zhao unit exceeds this number and will be ordered to downsize and conform. When Li's unit was commanded by Liu Zuozhou, it commanded four battalions, one cavalry unit, and one training unit, with more than three thousand officers, soldiers, and laborers, exceeding the provincial regulations by about a thousand people. Because there was no military pay, they extorted from the local population every day. After Liu's death, his nephew, Liu Lesan, using his qualification as the cavalry battalion commander, controlled Li Fengyun, and appointed himself as the deputy commander of the brigade. Secretary-General Zhang Weixiang also appointed himself as the brigade adjutant. The two jointly controlled Li, causing Li to be uneasy in his position. Recently, after Yin Rugeng negotiated with the Japanese, on September 30, he summoned Li to Tangshan and secretly conveyed the provincial government's order, formally appointing him as the commander of the 3rd Brigade. Li returned to Luan County defense area that night, gathered all the officers for a briefing, and mobilized the 1st Battalion to guard the entire city, announcing the provincial order, removing Liu Lesan and Zhang Weixiang from their positions. Liu's cavalry, one company caused a mutiny that day, fleeing towards the coast. Li immediately sent troops to pursue and encircle and monitor the remaining cavalry battalion to prevent any disturbances. On the morning of the 1st of this month, Liu Lesan was summoned by the Japanese military police in Shanhaiguan, who said that Liu was colluding with the old warlords such as Bai Jianwu, and detained him. Zhang Weixiang, seeing the situation was not good, was demoralized. However, the county town, both inside and outside, is still under guard and has not relaxed. As for the Feng Shoupeng unit, although it was previously decided to be reorganized into the 3rd Battalion, commanding four companies, under the control of the 5th Brigade under Li Yunsheng, due to the occurrence of the North China Incident, there was no time to discuss this. Currently, the unit and the Luo Dongshu unit have been stationed in Tangshan for a long time, and the defense area is both crowded and very inconvenient. Therefore, the Feng unit was transferred to Changping for defense, and the Luo unit was transferred to Shunyi for defense. The Feng unit was reorganized into a battalion as previously agreed, called the 3rd Battalion of the 5th Security Brigade, commanding mortar, machine gun, pistol, and cavalry, with a total of 317 officers and soldiers. On October 5, they moved to the defense area, turning onto the Zunping-Yu Road to Ping and marching on foot. The Luo Dongshu unit, called the Special Service Company of the 5th Security Brigade, with 220 men, after moving to the defense area, will be thoroughly downsized, allowing 120 men to remain, also under the direct command of Li Yunsheng. The Luo unit departed from Tangshan on September 29, sent to Ping by the Ping-Yu train, changed to the Ping-Sui train, got off at Kangzhuang, and marched on foot. In the future, Tangshan will still be defended by the Zhao Lei unit. (2nd)

The Yuehan Southern Railway: The Lechang-Pingshi Section is Open to Traffic

Goods from Guangdong can directly reach the Hunan border, benefiting commerce between Hunan and Guangdong

Guangzhou Dispatch. The north and south sections of the Yuehan Railway will soon be interconnected. At present, the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the project is being actively carried out. The Lechang-Pingshi section of the southern section has been completed on schedule and officially opened to traffic on the 24th of this month. Locomotives and passenger and freight cars are temporarily supplied by the Yuehan Southern Railway Bureau, and ticket sales are handled by the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Railway Bureau. Passengers and freight from Guangzhou to Pingshi must purchase separate tickets at Lechang. The fare from Lechang to Pingshi is 95 cents. After the completion of this section, goods from Guangdong Province can directly reach the Hunan border, which will greatly benefit commerce between Guangdong and Hunan. The transportation of goods from Guangdong to the Hunan border mainly consists of salt, textiles, and cloth. In recent years, due to the brisk sales of Huai salt in southern Hunan, the transportation of Guangdong salt to Hunan has decreased sharply, and the revenue of the railway bureau has also been affected. Last year, the railway's business revenue decreased by about 50,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The total revenue of the railway in the 23rd year is appended as follows: (1) Business revenue, transportation revenue, passenger business (passenger) 2,231,206 yuan 1 jiao 2 cents, (other) 328,083 yuan 1 jiao 2 cents, passenger business, (freight) 20,850,193 yuan 2 jiao 5 cents, freight business, (other) 1,136,609 yuan 7 cents, telegraph fee 725 yuan 4 jiao, total machinery plant profit 301 yuan 0 jiao 2 cents, rent 1,164 yuan 2 jiao 2 cents, miscellaneous 40,005 yuan, total of first category 4,462,868 yuan 7 jiao, total of second category 47,859 yuan 1 jiao 7 cents, total business revenue 45,100,727 yuan 9 jiao 4 cents. (2) Business expenses, general affairs fee 772,770 yuan 2 jiao, car affairs fee 404,254 yuan 3 jiao 8 cents, car affairs fee 945,541 yuan 0 jiao 1 cent, equipment maintenance fee 575,883 yuan 6 jiao 6 cents, total business expenses 3. Excluding expenses, the net profit of business revenue is 1,047,216 yuan 1 jiao 1 cent.

The Shanghai-Huzhou liner in Suzhou was robbed again

Chief Zhou of the Second District of the Water Police received a secret report that a large gang of lake bandits was lingering in Dongshan, Luzhi, and other places, plotting wrongdoing. He immediately ordered the Eighth Team to cooperate with the Zhaowu gunboat to search and suppress them separately. As the search was underway, news came that near Wujiagang, on the evening of the 3rd, a Shanghai-Huzhou liner was passing through the area when suddenly more than a dozen bandits came, carrying weapons to board the ship and rob the passengers. More than thirty passengers were not spared. After about an hour, the bandits left with their loot. After checking, the loss was about 2,000 yuan. At the time, the ship did not report to the police and went straight to Huzhou. The incident was within the jurisdiction of the Pingwang Public Security Sub-bureau, which immediately reported to the local water police and began to investigate. In addition, bandit traces were also found in the Taihu Lake area along the bottom of West Mountain. A stationed water police detachment has already been investigating. It is also heard that Chief Zhou, with the winter defense approaching in an instant, in order to maintain water security, will convene a meeting of the chiefs of each detachment within the day to discuss defense and bandit suppression issues.

Ningbo: The Old Jiang Bridge Can Be Completed This Year

The old Jiang Bridge between the Tongcheng District and Jiangdong in this port was contracted out last spring by foreign firms such as Siemens to rebuild a steel-concrete bridge, requiring 700,000 yuan. Construction began in June of last year, and the construction period was set at eighteen months. It can be completed and opened to traffic by the end of this year. The author believes that the progress of this bridge is of great concern to the people of Ningbo. On the 3rd, he went to the contracting company and the person in charge of the preparatory committee for the construction of the old Jiang Bridge to inquire about the latest construction situation. It was reported that the bridge piers on both sides had been completed long ago, and the bridge beams had also been erected. They are currently laying the iron plates on the bridge deck. Once the iron plate project is completed, the final project of paving and pouring cement on the bridge deck can be carried out. It is also said that the project can be completed as scheduled. At present, the construction details of the road surfaces at both ends of the bridge abutment have also been determined and will be started soon.

Aftermath of the Salt Folk Uprising in Yao County

The salt folk in Yuyao have been in constant disputes since the salt merchants stopped receiving and weighing salt, causing the salt folk to lose their livelihoods. After many days, the salt administration authorities repeatedly tried to mediate, ordering the salt merchants to receive salt at 60% of the original rate, starting on the 1st of this month. The matter had come to an end. However, on the morning of the 2nd, more than two thousand salt folk from Langxia Township in the county rushed to the township office to petition and to the office of the Ba長 to beg for food. The head of the township agreed to request Magistrate Lin on their behalf, and each person was given ten copper coins as snack money. The salt folk then dispersed.

The Municipal Party Headquarters of this city has determined that the 11th of this month will be the anniversary of the Premier's peril in the Chinese Embassy in London, England, while diligently pursuing the revolutionary movement. At that time, fortunately, Mr. Kandelay managed to rescue him and prevent him from being harmed. From then on, the Premier persevered and was able to promote the doctrine and recover the city. This year marks the 39th anniversary. The headquarters has specially formulated commemorative measures and will convene representatives from all organs, groups, schools, and party departments in the city at 10 a.m. that morning in the headquarters' auditorium for a memorial service. Member Lin Meiyan was elected as chairman of the assembly. The memorial measures are recorded as follows: (1) Convene representatives from all walks of life in Shanghai to hold the 39th anniversary commemoration of the Premier's peril in London. (2) Date: October 11, 10 a.m. (3) Venue: City Party Headquarters Auditorium. (4) The chairman of the assembly will be elected by the Municipal Executive Committee. (5) Starting from October 9, publish a notice in the newspaper for two days, informing (a) all organs and groups in the city to fly flags in commemoration, (b) each district party department and each district branch to send two representatives with letters to participate. (6) Issue a proclamation to the public on the 39th anniversary of the Premier's peril in London.

Italy Purchases Grain in Shanghai

One hundred tons will be shipped back on an Italian ship

Central News Agency reports that since the tension between Italy and Abyssinia, the price of rice and grain in this port has been rising daily, and it is rumored that Italy will purchase large quantities of grain in Shanghai. According to the export department of the shipping industry in this port, on the day of this month, the Italian ship Contessa Rosso will load 100 tons of grain when it departs from Shanghai to Italy.

Shen Shi News Agency reports that according to He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, the Italo-Abyssinian War has only been in local contact. The prices of our raw materials, such as cotton and wheat, have already risen. If the official war begins, our foreign trade will inevitably tend to two ways: (1) The export of raw materials and semi-finished products such as miscellaneous grains, such as cotton, wheat, rice, beans, oil cakes, and metals such as tungsten ore sand and antimony, will inevitably increase sharply, and prices will also rise accordingly. (2) However, if the war expands and the Mediterranean is blocked, cutting off our transportation to Europe, then not only will the export of raw materials and other items fail to be smooth, but it will fall into a state of stagnation. In short, this matter will have a huge impact on our international trade, but it may not be beneficial to us.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the Executive Yuan to Request Abolition of Guangdong Province's Special Agricultural Product Tax

Agricultural Product Tax is More Onerous Than Lijin, Merely Creating Opportunities for Foreign Merchants to Entice the People

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Guangdong Provincial Government to request the abolition of Guangdong Province's special agricultural product tax. (Details omitted) According to a letter from the Zalianghaoye Guild on the 3rd of this month and a letter from Guangdong merchants traveling in Shanghai on the 26th of this month, the special agricultural product tax, which originated in Guangdong Province, imposes heavy taxes on essential daily necessities, making it more onerous than lijin. When the bureau for collecting the tax was established, the Guangdong government claimed that it was to resist foreign goods and protect domestic products. However, the result is that foreign goods, those that evade and leak taxes, are still treated as domestic products, and the Guangdong government's revenue is limited, while Guangdong merchants and non-Guangdong merchants, Guangdong farmers and non-Guangdong farmers, all suffer. The Guangdong Provincial Special Tax Bureau taxes all kinds of goods, but apart from foreign rice, the main foreign goods are soybeans from the Northeast Provinces. However, the amount of oil and beans transported to Guangdong Province each year from Zhili, Shandong, Henan, Anhui, and Jiangsu is actually greater than that from the Northeast Provinces. If the same tax is levied, it would be equivalent to encouraging the import of Northeast soybeans and hindering the production and sales of goods from North and Central China. If products from non-Guangdong provinces are regarded as foreign goods, using tariff barriers to apply to one's own country is no different from severing one's own limbs. The Guangdong government is subordinate to the central government, and its policies should not be like this. If the provinces retaliate against each other, what kind of government will it be? Merchants should pay taxes according to regulations, and if it is beneficial to the country, they will do their best to contribute, even if the burden is slightly heavier. However, there are 20 to 30 foreign firms of a certain nationality that import and sell foreign rice without paying the special tax, and Chinese rice shops are almost all closed. The consulate of a certain country has also sent a special agent to clear customs and pick up goods on behalf of the foreign firms, claiming that the commercial treaty is not a tax rule promulgated by the central government, and does not pay various surcharges. Therefore, the Shantou Agricultural Product Special Tax Bureau collected more than 800,000 yuan in taxes per month, of which 400,000 to 500,000 yuan came from foreign rice. By the end of July this year, it collected more than 60,000 yuan, and by the end of August, it collected several thousand yuan. In this situation, foreign rice special tax will soon have no revenue to collect. Recently, some people have organized a joint-stock company to transport foreign rice and soybeans from the Northeast to Shantou. This means that the foreign soybean tax will soon have no revenue to collect. Shantou is like this, and Guangzhou is also like this. The facts are clear. The soybean tax will soon have nothing to collect except domestic products. Since the establishment of the Guangdong Provincial Special Tax Bureau, the tax on crude oil, soybean oil, and sesame oil has increased from 1.5 yuan to 5.4 yuan plus 10%, or 7.02 yuan in Guangdong currency, and the tax on soybeans, peanuts, sesame, and mountains has increased from 0.5 yuan to 1.8 yuan plus 30%, or 0.24 yuan in Guangdong currency. The tax rate is 30% to 40% or more of the value. Domestic oil and beans, burdened by this heavy tax, cannot compete with those from the three northeastern provinces that do not pay the special tax. In the future, those who are cunning will definitely seek refuge with foreign firms to evade taxes, and those who are honest will moan and eventually perish. At that time, the Guangdong government will only have an oppressive tax, which will cause suffering to merchants and farmers in various provinces, and will actually gain nothing. At this time of promoting domestic products and reviving rural areas, we are submitting this letter with the facts and requesting your association to investigate the above situation and forward it to the authorities in Nanjing and Guangdong to quickly find a way to maintain the situation and exempt the soybean and peanut special tax first, so that agricultural products from various provinces in the country can be freely transported to Guangdong for sale without being oppressed and manipulated by foreign merchants. This is to maintain national credibility, alleviate commercial difficulties, and would not only be a benefit to our industry, etc. The Association considered that the matter was closely related to its members and could not remain silent. It has always admired the leadership of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce in relieving the suffering of merchants, and hopes that you will sympathize with this request and forward it to the authorities in Nanjing and Guangdong, etc. After the lijin was abolished, provinces should no longer have the right to levy commodity taxes. This is a principle that must be strictly adhered to in order to maintain the unity of government orders. The Guangdong agricultural product special tax, in its nature, is a lijin in disguise, and its tax rate is even more burdensome than lijin. As costs increase, the burden on merchants becomes heavier. The honest people call out in vain and have no choice but to go bankrupt and close their businesses, while cunning people take refuge in foreign nationalities, causing the tax officials to turn a blind eye. This not only hinders national sovereignty and loses the people's hearts, but also destroys commerce, resulting in three harms at once. Merchants have been hoping for the abolition of lijin for decades, but they did not expect this tax system, which is more severe than lijin, to exist. It is truly regrettable. If we continue to maintain the current situation, it will only create opportunities for foreign merchants to entice the people. Public tax revenues will inevitably decrease day by day, and local disputes will be endless. What has happened in Shantou today is clear evidence of this. Therefore, it is better to adhere to the national order for the abolition of lijin and resolutely abolish it. We urge you to submit this telegram to the Council (Ministry) (Government) for review and approval and implementation. This would be to the benefit of the public. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. River.

Ministry of Railways Instructs Two Railway Bureaus to Negotiate Price Reductions for Wheat and Cotton Transport

Whether Price Reductions Will Actually Benefit Exports and Whether Merchants Are Willing to Purchase Domestic Products Are Also Questions

The Jinghu and Huning Railways Administration received a letter from Rong Zongjing requesting a reduction in freight rates for agricultural products such as wheat and cotton. They then submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways for instructions. The Ministry of Railways issued Instruction No. 8308: "Received your General Word No. 1521 of September 12, 1931. The Ministry has reduced the freight rates for agricultural products as much as possible in recent years, considering the impoverishment of the countryside. It has issued several orders to various railways to implement these reductions. Proposals have also been made at transportation conferences and joint transportation conferences. Regarding Rong Zongjing's request for a radical reduction in the freight rates for wheat and cotton by the Maoxin, Fuxin, and Shenxin General Companies, the railway has already inquired about it. It is feasible to conduct a detailed investigation of the production and sales of the various agricultural products for which the freight rate reduction is requested and then submit it to the Ministry for review. However, based on the past performance of various railways in reducing freight rates, it is doubtful whether reducing prices will actually benefit exports. Whether our country's ports and Shanghai merchants are willing to purchase domestic products is also a question. The prices of domestic raw materials are often higher and the quality is slightly lower, and they are mixed with mud, sand, and stones. It is also difficult to purchase them in large quantities, making it more difficult than purchasing imported goods. This has led to a sluggish domestic production and sales and the impoverishment of the rural economy. No matter how much freight rates are reduced or prices are lowered, there will be no market. This kind of phenomenon has become a serious domestic problem. If we do not find a way to remedy it, the harm will be immeasurable. Since the company is aware of this, it should pay close attention to it. In particular, the company itself should purchase raw materials from domestic sources as much as possible. Regarding the company's plan to purchase a certain number of tons of wheat and cotton in a certain location, when to transport it, and from which station to which station, what are the specific needs? If there are large purchases, and there are regular shipments every year or times when there is empty railway car availability, the railway should give as much assistance as possible. Please contact the company to discuss and implement the above specific measures. In addition, the railway should also take into account the direction of the railway's return empty cars and use this proposal to solve the problem of the railway's sluggish business. Please pay attention to this matter. This order."

Ministry of Finance Approves Clarification of Stamp Tax Application

Workers' Account Books and Folders Exempt from Stamps, Shipping Invoices Must Have Sufficient Stamps, Internal Documents Exempt from Stamps

Regarding questions about stamp tax, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce not only answered them at any time, but also submitted them to the Ministry for instructions. The Ministry approved and forwarded the information, and published the full text in the 9th issue of the Commercial Daily. Recently, it received Instruction No. 7298 from the Ministry of Finance: "Your telegram of August 30 has been received. The term (1) 'Workers' account books and folders used by workers to receive wages' refers to the books and folders issued by the factory to the workers so that they can receive their wages. It does not include the factory's own wage account books. If workers other than employees of the store also receive wages or remuneration from the store and the store issues books and folders for them to receive their wages, these books and folders can be handled in the same way. However, the store's own wage or remuneration account books should still be stamped in accordance with Article 11 of the tax rate table. (2) Although the distinction between shipping notes and shipping invoices is based on whether or not a transaction has been completed, only the shipping store and the customer know whether the goods have been sold and whether some of them have been returned. Since third parties cannot know this information, the shipping note, which lists the name, quantity, and value of the goods, is issued with the goods and is no different in nature from a shipping invoice. It should be stamped in accordance with the law to prevent taking advantage of loopholes. Article 5 of the Stamp Tax Law currently stipulates that documents subject to stamp tax should be stamped with stamp tax stamps upon delivery or use. Therefore, the stamps on this shipping note should be stamped at the time of issuance, based on the total amount listed on the note. (3) If the capital and business of a store's warehouse, manufacturing plant, distribution point, or branch are not independent, but are actually part of the same organization as the head office, the documents used for mutual notification that do not create external rights and obligations can be exempt from stamping. This has been previously approved and notified. As for restaurants and bars attached to department stores, if their capital and business are not independent from the company, the documents used for mutual notification that do not create external rights and obligations can be regarded as internal documents. Please be informed of this. This instruction."

Liquidation of Minghua Bank; Request to Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for Reconciliation

Chamber of Commerce Has Agreed to Accept; But Must Provide Complete Books and Records

Since Minghua Bank in this city announced its closure on May 23 of this year, Zhang Jiongbai, director and general manager of the bank, entrusted representatives to begin liquidating the bank's assets and debts. The Ministry of Finance also sent an supervisor. However, due to the economic downturn, the loans that had been made could not be recovered in a timely manner, resulting in a situation where the debts could not be paid off. Zhang Jiongbai, in accordance with Article 1, Paragraph 2 of the Bankruptcy Law, which came into effect on October 1, which stipulates that a debtor who stops payment is presumed to be unable to pay off debts, and Article 41 of the same law, which stipulates that a merchant who is unable to pay off debts may request reconciliation from the local chamber of commerce before filing a bankruptcy petition, provided that a petition for resolution has not been filed with the court, formally petitioned the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for reconciliation in accordance with the law. It is reported that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce stated that since the bank's main office is in Shanghai, it is in accordance with the law to request reconciliation, so there is no reason not to agree to it. However, in accordance with Article 7 of the same law, it is necessary to provide a truthful statement of assets, a list of creditors and debtors, and a guarantee to fulfill the proposed method of settlement, before it can be processed. A reply letter has been issued for your information.

Municipal Public Safety Bureau Extends Tea House Registration by One Month

Grace period extended to the end of this month; those who exceed the deadline will be dealt with according to the police regulations.

According to the Da Gong She, Cai Jinjun, the director of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau, stated that due to the proliferation of tea houses in the city, with both good and bad mixed together, some even engaging in gambling and associating with bandits, while generally neglecting cleanliness and tidiness, harming social order and public health, which is not a trivial matter. Therefore, he drafted tea house management regulations and organized tea house registration. Since the start of registration on August 1st of this year, as of the end of September, 544 tea houses have been registered and qualified. The original deadline was the end of September. However, since there are approximately over two thousand tea houses in the city, and only a quarter have registered, strict crackdown would be inconvenient. In order to accommodate business difficulties and show leniency, the bureau has specially extended the registration period by one month. Those who fail to register after the deadline will be dealt with strictly in accordance with Article 33 of the police regulations. A directive was issued yesterday to all branch bureaus to instruct tea house owners in their respective jurisdictions to come to the bureau for registration within the month. The original directive stated: "The revised tea house management regulations of this city have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation. It is now found that many tea houses have come to the bureau to apply for registration and licenses, but many have delayed registration. The deadline is set at the end of October. Those tea houses that fail to register after the deadline shall be dealt with according to regulations. In addition to separate orders, the branch bureau chief is hereby ordered to comply, instruct the subordinates to separately notify and inform, and not to delay, so as to avoid punishment. Sincerely, Director Cai Jinjun."

Iranian Mirek Sues French Tram Company

Judgment: Compensation for the Plaintiff's Losses

According to the Da Mei Evening News, Mirek, an Iranian (Persian), fell and was injured on May 4th when disembarking from a tram on Avenue Joffre because the iron gate was still open while the tram had already started moving. He sued the ticket seller in the Second Special District Court for dereliction of duty, because the bell was rung and the tram was started before the iron gate was closed. The court sentenced him to a fine of ten yuan. Mirek then filed a lawsuit with the French Consulate against the French Concession Tram Company, demanding compensation for losses. The defendant's lawyer argued that the company could not be held responsible without definite proof of negligence, and the judgment of the Chinese court could not be used to sue the French company. The presiding judge stated that since the person employed by the defendant had already received criminal punishment, the defendant could not evade responsibility, and therefore ruled that the French tram company should compensate the plaintiff for losses of 1,970 yuan.

Rickshaw Guild Petitions Public Safety Bureau to Investigate and Punish Car Thieves

The rickshaw industry guild believes that stealing cars for ransom is extremely harmful to rickshaw pullers, so it has established a "no-ransom" group. Car owners who pay five cents per car per month, if their car is stolen while the rickshaw puller is working and the investigation confirms it, will only be required to pay six yuan. If the car is recovered but the rubber tires have been removed, three yuan will be refunded. If all parts are complete, no payment will be required. All losses such as new tires and car rental fees will be compensated by the guild. As a result, for several months, the thieves who used to demand ransoms have almost disappeared, and the rickshaw pullers have benefited a lot. Recently, these thieves have been secretly active again, trying to disrupt this organization. The rickshaw guild has petitioned the Public Safety Bureau to investigate.

Yuanyuan Farm Suddenly Declares Liquidation Yesterday

Yuanyuan Farm Co., Ltd., located on the Great Western Road in this city, the largest dairy farm run by Chinese people, suddenly entrusted lawyers Qiu Hanping and Song Yunhui, and accountants Zhao Yaojing and Liu Konggui to announce liquidation yesterday. The details are as follows:

Yuanyuan Farm, with a capital of 500,000 yuan, began operations in the summer of 1932. It was founded by He Lin and Yuan and was registered by the Ministry of Industry with a capital of 500,000 yuan. It raises the world's best dairy cows, with the aim of improving Chinese cattle breeds and producing condensed milk. The internal equipment, such as disinfection machines, cattle-making methods, mechanical milking, cattle hygiene, cold storage rooms, and chemical rooms, are all excellent and perfect, and nothing is unscientific. It produces and sells milk, milk essence, milk fat, and manufactures condensed milk daily, employing hundreds of workers. The scale of construction is grand and beautiful, and it can be called the leader of the dairy industry in Shanghai. Last year's business reached more than 10,000 yuan per month.

Reason for Liquidation: Since the farm was involved in litigation with Jin Cheng Bank, there have been increasing troubles and its business has plummeted, making it impossible to maintain. The shareholders' meeting on the 19th of last month decided to liquidate. However, the farm's cattle cannot be left without someone responsible for them for even a day. It is said that the liquidators have separately sought solutions and submitted them to the High Court for instructions. The farm has debts of over 500,000 yuan, but the company's assets are worth over 600,000 yuan. Outstanding debts from customers are also over 100,000 yuan, which can be used for clearing and offsetting.

Animal Protection Society Holds Propaganda Rally Yesterday

Chairman Ye Gongchuo reports on the significance of animal protection; Guan Jiongzhi and Tong Hangbai both deliver stern speeches; The entire city obeys the order to stop slaughtering for one day.

Yesterday (the 4th) was World Animal Day, the 101st anniversary. The Shanghai China Animal Protection Society held a propaganda rally to protect animals and solicit members at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at Tianhou Palace Bridge at 1:00 PM. At the same time, major newspapers published special issues, city radio stations broadcast speeches on the significance of animal protection, all trams posted propaganda slogans, and the entire country complied with the central government's order to stop slaughtering for one day. The details are as follows:

Venue Arrangement

The rally venue was located at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at Tianhou Palace Bridge. The Party and national flags were crossed at the entrance, and a white cloth banner reading "China Animal Protection Society Animal Department and Propaganda Rally to Solicit Members" was hung high. Next to it was a large painting specially made by the society. Upon entering, the corridors on both sides and the four walls of the venue were filled with eye-catching animal protection slogans and paintings. The entrance to the auditorium was designated as a signing area, and the podium was located in the center. The same banner was hung on the podium, with a portrait of the Premier and the Party and national emblem above. A reporter's seat was set up below, with a record seat on the left and a band seat on the right. The rest were guest seats. The venue was maintained by members of the Buddhist Association's Boy Scout Service Corps and the Youth Association's Middle School Boy Scouts. The Longhua Orphanage band performed music at the venue. The arrangement was simple and solemn.

Participating Representatives

Attendees included: Chairman Ye Gongchuo, Director Kong Xiangxi (represented by Zeng Kezhai), Wang Xiaolai, Zhong Ketuo, Li Jingwei, Public Security Bureau Chief Cai Jinjun (represented by Dong Xianxiang), Health Bureau Chief Li Yanan (represented by Wang Junchang), Tong Hangbai from the Municipal Party Department, Rao Qiangsheng from the Social Bureau, Guan Jiongzhi and Zhao Puchu from the Chinese Buddhist Association, Master Taixu, Dharma Master Dabeizhai, Dharma Master Lalai from India and Ceylon, Miss Belle, representative of the Western Animal Protection Society, Qian Huafo, Huang Jingwan, Shen Tianxin, Chen Gang from the Postal Service Association, students from Renhui Elementary School, and over 600 guests from all walks of life. The presidium included Kong Xiangxi, Ye Gongchuo, Wang Xiaolai, Guan Jiongzhi, and Dun Ketuo. The master of ceremonies was Pan Renwei.

(Qichang's photo) Animal Protection Day Solicitation Meeting

Chairman's Report

After the opening ceremony and formal etiquette, Chairman Ye Gongchuo gave an opening speech: "Distinguished guests, fellow members, today is World Animal Day. Our society is taking this opportunity to raise national awareness of animal protection. The main purpose of World Animal Day is that humans should be kind to animals. Although animals' abilities are not as good as humans', humans should not abuse them as much as possible because of this. Over the past few decades, many philanthropists and scholars around the world have felt from academic and conceptual perspectives that animals cannot protect themselves and that humans should protect them. Therefore, various countries in the world have joint animal protection organizations. Our country has only had such organizations for two years. Although most people in society sympathize, there are also many who are indifferent. This is due to the general lack of in-depth understanding of animal protection among our compatriots. Over the past year, the number of people who sympathize with our society's purpose has gradually increased, and people sympathize and arouse social attention, understand the meaning of animal protection through attention, and the public opinion expresses enthusiasm sympathy. In addition to today's commemoration, we are also holding a membership solicitation meeting. Major newspapers are also strongly supporting us, and our society is deeply pleased. Moreover, the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior have responded to our society's request and issued a clear order to ban slaughter throughout the country for one day. This is not only the government's expression of sympathy and importance, but also assistance, which is especially fortunate. However, what our society should do has not been fully realized due to various difficulties. I hope that all enthusiastic people will work together to help our society complete its mission."

Guan Jiongzhi's Speech

Recently, many people feel that the world is now a world where people kill each other. The panic among human beings is getting worse every day. We ourselves do not have enough time, so how can we talk about protecting other animals? This statement seems very right, but it is actually wrong. We have at least two reasons to answer them: First, human beings are intelligent and capable animals. When they are oppressed by the environment, they can use their own strength to protect themselves. The intelligence and ability of other animals are much worse than that of human beings. When they are harmed by humans, they can only suffer in silence and cannot resist. Although animals have different levels of intelligence and ability, the value of life is the same. Therefore, these weak lives need human protection. Second, human beings' habit of harming animals is the main reason for cultivating human beings' mutual killing. It will definitely cause a bad outcome of world unrest. It is like a child who kills insects from an early age and will easily kill birds, cats, dogs, and even people when they grow up, without feeling surprised. Therefore, the fundamental way to seek human peace is to first transform human psychology. A few years ago, the chairman of the European Vegetarian Society said a sentence. He said, "If you want the world not to bleed, start with not bleeding from our dining table." This sentence is very meaningful. I think that people who are enthusiastic about world peace should not disagree with this fundamental method.

Report on the Society's Name

Next, Director Li Jingwei reported on the society's affairs. A. Organization: (1) Actively seek to strengthen strength and start soliciting members. (2) Plan to establish local branches. Two branches have been established in Xi'an and Chang'an in Shaanxi Province, and branches are being prepared in Peiping, Changsha, Suzhou, and other places. B. Propaganda: (1) In addition to holding propaganda rallies once a year, we have first obtained the consent of the Xinwen Bao to publish special issues of our society irregularly. Other newspapers are in contact. (2) This summer, we specially printed 10,000 animal protection text and picture fans and distributed them to all walks of life. (3) From April 8th to 13th this year, the association joined the Western Anti-Cruelty to Animals Association to hold Animal Protection Propaganda Week. C. Career: Prohibit the killing of draft cattle in various places. In addition, prohibit the killing of field frogs and stray dogs, and request the Executive Yuan to issue an order to ban slaughter throughout the country today.

Tong Hangbai's Speech

Next, Zhang Hangbai, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, saying: "Although the four words 'animal protection' seem to have been heard only in recent years, our country has long had the idea of ​​animal protection, that is, the principle of loyalty and forgiveness said by Confucius, and the spirit of benevolence said by Premier Sun. Animal protection is a moral issue in meaning and a human evolution issue in history. Why should we protect animals? Because humans love life and are afraid of death, and animals also love life and are afraid of death. Humans seek to prolong life, and so do animals. In terms of morality, humans love and protect themselves and extend this to animals. Mencius said, 'Sufficient kindness is enough to protect life.' Love for relatives and benevolence is one principle. From the perspective of human evolution, the way of life of human beings in the barbaric era in the past was struggle and killing. In today's civilized era of the 20th century, human beings' way of life should be rationally reformed. Although Animal Day originated in Europe and the United States, our country has long had this idea. In the future, we hope that there will be rational life and mutual love between human beings, and that this will be extended to animals." There were also speeches by Wang Junchang of the Health Bureau, Dharma Master Lalai, and Belle, representative of the Western Animal Protection Society, with different meanings and from different perspectives.

Guests' Speeches

Next, people from all walks of life gave speeches. Wang Xiaofan's speech said that humans are one of the animals and the spirit of all things, but people should not kill other animals because they are the spirit of all things. Therefore, protecting animals is a morality that humans should fulfill. If we can protect animals, there will be no killing in the world in the future. Ceylonese Dharma Master Nilai Dan's speech said that most of the members of the Animal Protection Association are Buddhists, which is what I like the most. In the teachings of various religions in the world, there is a common understanding of animal protection. Take Confucius, who is worshiped by the Chinese, for example, he also has many famous sayings about animal protection. We hope that the world can have practical measures for animal protection, and the happiness of human beings will be increased. Finally, Master Taixu gave a speech, saying that animal protection is extremely important in Buddhism. In Buddhist scriptures, animals are called sentient beings. The so-called sentient beings are creatures with emotions. All animals have the psychology of avoiding death and loving life, hating labor and loving leisure, so how can we impose on animals what we cannot bear ourselves? Therefore, I hope that all sectors of society can understand this situation and that all human beings will have the psychology of animal protection.

Zhong's Reply

Finally, Director Zhong Ketuo gave a speech, saying: "Today, we are honored to have Party and government officials send personnel to guide us, and guests from all walks of life come to participate. We are also honored and grateful to have Dharma Master Lalai, representative of the Buddhist Association of India and Ceylon, and Miss Belle, representative of the Western Animal Protection Society, come to guide us. Our association will continue to work with this purpose and hope that all parties will be enthusiastic and supportive and give us guidance at any time." Finally, the entire group took a group photo, and then began performing entertainment, including the Postal Workers' Union's national music performance, Renhui Elementary School's opera, and the songs and dances of Bai Hong and Li Mingjian of the Mingyue Opera Troupe, which were very wonderful and won a lot of applause. The meeting ended with music at 7:00 PM.

Former Zhejiang Party Committee Member Li Chaoying Awarded British Doctorate

Only Two Doctoral Degrees Awarded by London University Only Li is of Chinese Nationality

Mr. Li Chaoying, the former Executive Committee Member and Training Minister of the Zhejiang Provincial Party, was sent to study in the United States by the Zhejiang Provincial Government in the 19th year of the Republic (1930). He then studied economics at the University of London. He briefly returned to China to attend the National Congress. After the meeting, he continued his studies abroad for a total of five years. This summer, he obtained a Doctorate in Economics from the University of London. His dissertation is approximately six hundred pages and over two hundred thousand words. The university has approved its publication. Only two students from the University of London were awarded doctorates in economics this year. Only Li is of Chinese nationality. Doctoral degrees from around the world are considered most difficult to obtain in England. This is the first time that a Chinese student's dissertation has been approved for publication by the University of London. Mr. Li has many friends in China, who have sent congratulatory letters and telegrams. It is said that after the publication of his dissertation, Mr. Li plans to travel to the United States, France, Germany, and Italy for a week of inspections before returning to China, which is expected to be in the spring of the 25th year of the Republic (1936).

Former Journalist of This Newspaper Xie Fusheng Passes Away

He Leaves Behind Two Sons and Three Daughters in Poverty Chinese and Western Communities Mourn Upon Hearing the News

Mr. Xie Fusheng, a well-known translator, recently founded the English-language "Fu Sheng Times" and the Fu Sheng Commercial English Evening School at 505 Henan Road, Jin Xing Building in this city. He personally managed these ventures, which were highly praised by all sectors of society. Unexpectedly, Mr. Xie recently suffered from overwork and the adverse weather, leading to an acute case of typhoid fever. Despite medical treatment from both Chinese and Western doctors, he passed away yesterday afternoon at 2:10 PM at his residence at 43 Gao Fu Lane, Avenue Sainte-Marie in the French Concession. His remains have been transported to the Shanghai Funeral Parlor by his family and will be formally entombed today. Mr. Xie was not good at accumulating wealth, so his death leaves his family in dire poverty. He leaves behind a wife, two sons, and three daughters. The eldest son, Guanghan, assists with the newspaper business at home. The second son, Guangdui, is studying in Hong Kong. The third son is still young. The eldest daughter, Minzhen, also assists her father in running the newspaper. The second daughter stays at home to assist her mother with needlework. The youngest daughter is studying at the Taoist temple in Hong Kong. Mr. Xie was a native of Nanhai, Guangdong, but grew up in Shandong. His wife, Ms. Liu, is also a native of Guangdong, but grew up in Shanghai. The couple had a very close relationship and had ten children together, four of whom have already passed away, leaving only six survivors. Mr. Xie graduated from St. Francis Xavier's College with a deep understanding of English. He served as a reporter for the Che Bao and the Continental Daily News. When Sun Chuanfang was the Commander-in-Chief of the Five-Province Allied Army, the English-language Public Opinion Newspaper, founded by Mr. Xie, angered Sun Chuanfang due to its strong criticism. He was arrested and interrogated at the military headquarters by Li Baozhang (then the Garrison Commander of Shanghai and Wusong), nearly facing misfortune. Fortunately, through the efforts of Yu Qiaqing and others in Shanghai, he was saved from death, but remained in prison for a long period. He was only able to regain his freedom after the National Revolutionary Army advanced north and Sun Chuanfang was defeated. Mr. Xie's lifelong ambition was to dedicate himself to the newspaper industry. Therefore, he recently used his personal resources to found the English-language Fu Sheng Times and the Fu Sheng Commercial English Evening School. Just as he was about to realize his ambitions, he contracted a minor illness and suddenly passed away. Mr. Xie had many friends in Chinese and Western communities, and all were filled with sorrow and grief upon hearing this tragic news.

Entomologist Discusses Malaria Prevention in Minhang

Using Suffocation Methods to Eradicate Avoiding the Spread to Shanghai

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Health Department has already issued warnings to citizens about the prevalence of malaria in Minhang and other areas. A reporter from Datong News Agency, through the introduction of Mr. Zhang Jingou, Chief of the Plant Pest and Insect Group of the Commodity Inspection Bureau, interviewed an entomologist who has special knowledge of mosquitoes. He provided a detailed account of the prevention methods. A summary is provided below.

Characteristics of Anopheles Mosquitoes

The spread of malaria is due to the transmission of malarial parasites by Anopheles mosquitoes, which is well known. The morphology of Anopheles mosquitoes can be identified by the following features: the palps of both males and females are nearly equal to or exactly equal to the length of the proboscis. The proboscis extends forward in a straight line with the body axis. When resting, they often form an angle with the surface they are on. On a vertical wall, the angle is approximately thirty degrees. The wings have spots. They fly silently.

No Danger to This City

Since the outbreak of malaria in Minhang, people in this port have been deeply concerned about being infected. In fact, Anopheles mosquitoes are not good at flying. Usually, they do not fly more than one hundred yards. There have been no reports of Anopheles mosquitoes flying over one mile. The distance between this port and Minhang is more than one mile. Knowing this, it is clear that this port will not be affected by the Anopheles mosquitoes from Minhang, and our health will not be harmed.

Prevention Methods

There are many methods of prevention. The most simple and easy to implement in rural environments is to scatter wood shavings, bran, or rice husk ash into various polluted waters. This can suffocate the Anopheles larvae or mosquito larvae. It can also stop the mosquitoes from laying eggs. As for the treatment of malaria, the administration of quinine pills to kill the parasites is best. Those who have not been infected and those who have been infected should pay attention to isolation, which is true for all common diseases and need not be reiterated.

Absurd Deception by a Russian One Yuan Can Be Transformed into Two Yuan

Jiang Shuling Commits Suicide After Being Deceived into Debt The Rogue Russian and Accomplices Have All Been Arrested

The Russian Yino Gendi Xuema Lafoma Lengshi, residing at No. 38, Lane 1025, Jing'an Temple Road, Shanghai West, does not engage in honest work but specializes in fraud for a living. Sun Shanpu, residing at No. 3, Rongqing Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, acts as his accomplice. All Chinese nationals who are deceived by the Russian national are induced by Sun and his Guizhou friend, Ye Xiangsheng. Recently, the Russian used a trick that could turn one yuan into two yuan to entice people, with Sun luring victims. Sun then instructed Ye to lure Jiang Shuling from Anhui to Sun's house on August 12. Jiang, initially unaware of the fraud, handed over 30 yuan in banknotes. When he returned the next day, they returned 45 yuan to him. In just one night, he made a 50% profit. Jiang was overjoyed and regretted not investing more capital. If not, wealth could be quickly attained. The group, seeing Jiang's intention, took the opportunity to encourage him. Jiang agreed to raise more funds. He borrowed from all sides. Within three days, he went to the Russian's residence with a hundred yuan and handed over all his money. When he returned the next day, thinking he would easily get 150 yuan, the Russian initially used excuses to stall and then falsely claimed that the raw materials needed for the transformation had been used up and the money was used to purchase the materials. To get more he needed another eighty yuan. Otherwise, there would be no offspring. But Jiang was penniless. He could only return dejectedly. Later, he repeatedly demanded repayment but was not repaid. The creditors were pressing him harder every day. With no way out, he went to the North Railway Station Hotel in the French Concession on September 3 and committed suicide by taking poison in a room. He left a letter to his uncle, Wang Ruixiang, stating the reason for his suicide. When the hotel owner discovered it, he immediately reported it to the police, who sent an ambulance to the hospital, but it was too late to save him. He died. It was immediately reported to the First Special District Local Court, which commissioned a prosecutor to inspect the body and ordered Ruixiang to prepare the coffin. At that time, Ye Xiangsheng was still unaware that Jiang had committed suicide out of anger. A few days ago, he even went to Jiang Ruixiang's house at No. 27, Fuqing Lane, Tiantong Road, to visit Shuling, only to learn that he had caused the disaster. Ye, feeling responsible for Jiang's death, volunteered to help find Sun. He then led detectives from the French Concession Police to arrest Sun Shanpu. They then apprehended the Russian. Under interrogation, it was discovered that the fraud took place in the Public Concession. The French Concession Police transferred all the suspects to the First Special District Local Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang interrogated them. Qian Xunjiu, the lawyer for the Shanghai Municipal Council, presented the case and requested that they be punished in accordance with Article 339 of the Criminal Code. When questioned, the defendants shifted responsibility to each other. However, they all confessed to the fact that the Russian had given Sun 30 yuan after obtaining the money, and Sun had then given Ye 10 yuan. The court stated that the case still required investigation and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for further interrogation at a later date.

The income was handed over to Wangshi for registration in the ledger. If she did not get her way, she would be beaten, etc. When interrogated, Yan Wangshi claimed that Wang Xiaohong had been introduced by her sisters to rent a small house, and she volunteered to be a prostitute, and it was not forced by the woman. This time, she broke a pot, so she was slightly blamed. The rest of the confession was vague. Judge Qiu sentenced Yan Wangshi to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 100 yuan for intending to profit and inducing women from good families to commit adultery. Wang Xiaohong was fined five yuan for violating the regulations on private prostitution and sent to the Women and Children's Association for custody.

The wife and concubine of Lin Yuting, a returning overseas student from the United States, lived in Shanghai. A few years ago, Lin died of illness. Her mother lived in a western-style house and drove a car, forcing the plaintiff out and not providing living expenses. For this reason, she requested that the husband's inheritance be allocated to her so that she could live. After receiving the complaint, the court summoned them. Yesterday afternoon at 1:30, Judge Feng opened the court for summons. The plaintiff Lin Jiangsong arrived at the court with lawyer Li Ming and stated the situation. Republic Road Robbery Case

Weng Bingji Robbed of Silver Dollars

Weng Bingji, a Ningbo native carpenter residing above the Xin Chi Bathhouse entrance on Republic Road near Yongxing Road in Zhabei, had previously collected sixty-one silver dollars in wages from the factory. This sum included five ten-dollar notes from the Central Bank and twelve silver dollars. He carried it home in his wallet and placed it in the dressing table drawer in his room. Unexpectedly, at around 11:00 AM, Weng went to work at the factory, leaving his wife alone at home. A robber, appearing to be in his twenties, wearing a short linen shirt and blue cloth trousers, came upstairs under the pretext of looking for "Xiao Agen." Seeing his suspicious demeanor, Weng's wife replied that no one of that name lived there. The robber then dragged Weng's wife into the room, saying, "Sister-in-law, please help me." He then opened the drawer and, seeing fifty dollars in banknotes and silver in the wallet, took it and put it in his pocket. There were also twelve silver dollars wrapped in paper. The robber took seven dollars and left five. He then dragged Weng's wife to a small room at the back, locked the door from the outside, and fled. By the time Weng's wife managed to open the door, the robber had disappeared.
