Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

Electronic Alarm

— Zhong Xu

(Electronic Alarm)

This device is made of a few simple parts and is a very interesting game. It can be used to prevent people from approaching an area, causing a bell to ring or a warning light to turn on. It can also be used to prevent fires and report rain.

The search wire can be connected in two ways: connected to point X is more stable and does not have the problem of radiating radio waves. Connecting to point Y is more sensitive.

(1) Connected to point X First, adjust the absorption circuit L1C1 to the same wavelength as the oscillation circuit LC. Move L very far away, and the regeneration circuit will start to oscillate. Connect a 10-10MA ammeter in series at point X in the diagram. At this time, the screen current is approximately four thousandths of an ampere. Then move L1 closer to L, increasing the coupling degree. The original oscillation of LC decreases. The tighter the coupling, the weaker the oscillation, until it is completely extinguished. At this time, the screen current is approximately seven thousandths of an ampere. Therefore, oscillation does not normally occur, and there is no interference from radiated radio waves. If the search wire is wound around the room (assuming a room is being secured), if someone approaches, the capacitance between the search wire and the ground will increase. The wavelength in the absorption circuit will naturally increase, and the absorption will decrease, causing the regeneration circuit to oscillate again, and the screen current will return to four thousandths of an ampere. This change can cause the relay to open and close, and connecting a light or alarm bell to the relay output point will trigger an alarm.

(2) Connected to point Y Adjust the regeneration circuit to a wavelength slightly shorter than the absorption circuit. Although the coupling between the two circuits is very tight, oscillation still occurs normally. When the search wire is affected, the regeneration circuit increases the wavelength, matching the absorption circuit, and the oscillation stops, causing the screen current to change and trigger the alarm.

If you want to use it to report rain, simply place a pole outside the window with a metal plate on top, and another plate on top of that, insulated with Bakelite. One plate is grounded, and the other is connected to point X or Y. When it rains, the capacitance increases and triggers the device. To use it to prevent fire, use a water thermometer, with one end wrapped in tin foil up to 70 degrees Fahrenheit and the other end wrapped in tin foil from 900 degrees Fahrenheit to the top. The lower end is grounded, and the upper end is connected to point X or Y. When a fire starts, the temperature rises, and the mercury column rises, increasing the capacitance between the two pieces of tin foil and triggering the device. It can also be used in other places, as long as it is legal.

The following parts are used:

LL1 18-gauge double-layer silk-covered wire, wound 10 turns on a 2-inch diameter Bakelite form.

L2 30-gauge lacquered wire wound 4 turns on a tube, with a distance of 1/2 inch from the L end.

CC1 .0003 MFD.

C2 .0001 MFD.

C3 .01 MFD

R 100000

V Type 31

A Electric two-volt

W Electric ninety-volt

Electric Organ

— Yong Yan

Although the structure of current organs is already sophisticated, there are still various shortcomings in practice. For example, the sound does not play immediately after the key is pressed, the volume is too small, there are too few types of timbres (ToneClolr), the range of volume change is too small, and smooth control is not possible. All these have long been desired to be solved but cannot.

The "Electric Organ" completely uses the principle of electricity, so the sound can be played immediately after the key is pressed, and the accuracy and beauty of the sound are completely unmatched by ordinary organs. Moreover, it uses a sound frequency amplifier, so the sound can be arbitrarily amplified to various degrees, and at the same time has extremely smooth volume control.

See the attached diagram for the sound generation principle of this electric organ. The "tone plate" in the diagram is connected to a synchronous motor and rotates at a constant speed. The plate has several protrusions. When these protrusions pass by the electromagnet next to it, the magnetic lines of force change. At this time, the coil on the electromagnet is induced to generate a sound frequency voltage of equal frequency. This sound frequency voltage is amplified and can drive the speaker to generate sound. This sound-generating organization is shared by 91 groups in the whole machine to generate various kinds of different timbres. The external shape of the electric organ is the same as that of the ordinary organ, and the playing method is also the same as that of the ordinary organ.

Eliminating the shortcomings of regenerative radios

— Juan

The regenerative radio that we usually call is a device that feeds back a part of the high-frequency current in the plate circuit of the detection vacuum tube to the grid circuit through a regenerative coil to increase the amplification. If this method is not handled properly and the degree of regeneration is exceeded, it will interfere with other people's radio reception and make the sound quality worse. This is a well-known phenomenon, but this shortcoming is not without a way to eliminate it. Now I will introduce a method to eliminate it:

The elimination method is to use another so-called inverse regeneration coil and a series of variable capacitors, and apply appropriate adjustments to remove the excessive effect of regeneration.

The attached diagram (1) is the detection vacuum tube of the regenerative radio, (2) is the plate circuit, (3) is the cathode circuit, and a fixed capacitor (4), a variable capacitor (5), and a common regenerative coil (6) are arranged between the plate and cathode circuits. In addition, an inverse regeneration coil (7) with the opposite excitation direction and a measuring capacitor are added in parallel with it.

Shen Bao Wireless Weekly Department

Publishing World

After reading "A Collection of Studies on Chinese Field Systems"

— Ge Man

In the twenty-fifth issue of the Publishing World, I saw Mr. Zeng Jianping's reading of "A Collection of Studies on Chinese Field Systems." I read it carefully and learned that Mr. Zeng Jianping spent a full ninety cents to buy a new book "A Collection of Studies on Chinese Field Systems" written by Mr. Chen Boying, published by the Commercial Press. After reading this book, he cried bitterly and said, "I can only feel the pain in my heart," because the citations, structure, and conclusions in this book are plagiarized from Mr. Chen Dengyuan's book "Chinese Land System," and it is used as a blueprint.

I have not read these two books, but I do know something about the authors of the two books. It turns out that Mr. Chen Boying and Mr. Chen Dengyuan are both from Zhouxing Town in Yuyao. Because they teach in universities in Nanjing, they are, of course, "extraordinary" people in our Yuyao. In conversations between friends, they often mention these two gentlemen. I seem to have heard that Mr. Chen Boying teaches in universities in Nanjing and has written books on Chinese land issues; Mr. Chen Dengyuan also teaches in universities in Nanjing and has also written books on Chinese land issues. At that time, I had some speculation that there are many Chinese names, perhaps Mr. Chen Boying knew that Mr. Chen Dengyuan was "two in one"? Now that I have read Mr. Zeng's article, I asked my friend and learned that my guess was correct.

Therefore, I feel that today's writers and publishers only aim to seek harmony and ignore the mission of promoting culture. According to Mr. Zeng's article, "Chen Dengyuan's work was published in 1932, while Chen Boying's work was only published this year... Those who are knowledgeable may have the same opinions, but they cannot even have the same references and conclusions. Moreover, not only one chapter is the same, but other sections are also mostly the same." From this point of view, Mr. Chen Dengyuan has no new opinions and insights to contribute since 1932; he just changed his appearance, changed some content, and published another book; but the preface says: "The collection of studies on field systems is the result of my historical research in the past two or three years." In this way, what is the purpose of publishing Jia's collection of studies on field systems? It is very obvious.

I hope that writers and publishers will look at the backward Chinese culture and listen to the cry of "I can only feel the pain in my heart."

On Small Newspapers

— Xu Lu

There is a noteworthy phenomenon in the recent publishing world: the rise of small newspapers. Dozens of small newspapers have sprung up one after another; and judging from the situation, they will probably become more prosperous and more numerous in the future.

Frankly speaking, this seems to be a gratifying phenomenon; China's newspapers are not as numerous as those in the West, not to mention the West, but even Japan. Newspapers are the best weapon for public education—their importance is not limited to conveying news; now that they can gradually increase, it also strengthens the power of public education. Naturally, it is extremely gratifying.

But in more detail, whether or not there is an effect in running any kind of cultural enterprise is not just a matter of quantity. It is not enough to say that more is good, it should also have substantial quality. Quality and quantity should be equally important; for example, in the case of newspapers, if the quality is good but the quantity is not large, its power is certainly limited; if the quantity is large but the quality is not good, then not only will there be no effect, but it may even become a toxin, because its quantity is large and it is more widely distributed to the minds of the public, achieving the opposite effect of the newspaper's original meaning.

Therefore, when we see the vigorous rise of small newspapers, we cannot simply congratulate the publishing world for this, but we should also look at the substance of these newspapers with a solemn eye.

The power of so-called "small newspapers" in Shanghai (in fact, in the entire province of Jiangsu) is known to everyone. The number of readers and the good sales are really no less than those of large newspapers. The general literate public, except for a small number of students and the upper intellectual class, everyone would rather read small newspapers than large newspapers. What is the reason for this? After investigation, there are probably the following reasons:

1. Because small newspapers are cheap. It also saves time to read,

2. Because the content of small newspapers is suitable for the psychology of the general public, interesting, novel, police-like, obscene, and sometimes publishes news that large newspapers dare not publish (because of this, there was a cry that small newspapers were more truthful than large newspapers in the past), as well as rumors that are enough to stimulate ordinary people.

3. Small newspapers not only provide news facts (of course, a small number), but also provide interest, so people are happy to get both.

For these reasons, small newspapers sell better than large newspapers, and general newspaper merchants are naturally very enthusiastic about publishing them. Although some also rise and fall with life and death, they are still gradually increasing. Some small newspapers have a long history and are deeply rooted.

From the above reasons, it can be seen that the demonstration newspaper does have its own characteristics that attract people. If it can be run from the starting point of the fundamental meaning of the news business, then the welfare given to the public is certainly indelible. But unfortunately, the general so-called small newspapers only focus on the purpose of speculation and profit, and also because most of the editors are people of the old era, the content (that is, the substance) is made very bad, containing a lot of toxic substances. These bad substances not only give the public a bad tendency, but also invisibly affect the future of the news business. We only need to look at the old-fashioned, strong low-level tastes, boring and even rogue nature of those small newspapers, and the lack of educational significance, and we can understand how great a bad influence they have on people (not only readers).

Therefore, it is very necessary and inevitable to create new small newspapers to replace those old ones. Newspaper popularization and newspaper cheapening are the fundamental meaning and goal of starting small newspapers. In other words, to achieve that, the form of small newspapers is very adoptable.

But we must pay attention to the motive for starting the journal. This is very important. To make newspapers cheaper and more popular is certainly one of the motives for starting small newspapers. But I think what is more important is: at this time of transition between new and old small newspapers, the new small newspapers should bear a revolutionary responsibility, and the new small newspapers should be different from the old small newspapers, and strive to make their content new, modern, substantial, and have educational significance... By using this method of reform, the old small newspapers will be invisibly hit, causing the corrupt ones to be abandoned by readers and eliminated, losing their ability to release poison.

This is a destructive attitude, but destruction is necessary for construction. Naturally, conversely, to make this destructive attitude effective, it is also necessary to first build up one's own substance.

Now let's take a look at the current new small newspapers, what is their motive, and what is their substance?

The slogan of newspaper popularization has been shouted out. Some even "aim to sell millions per day." This, of course, is correct. In order to allow more people to read newspapers (although to put it bluntly, it is also to make themselves get more of the price of running a newspaper), it was the original meaning of running a newspaper, but as far as I can see, there is no one who can take the kind of destructive motive I mentioned above and use it as one of the goals.

This can be seen from the content of most newly published small newspapers. Naturally, some have also been reformed - for example, changing the text to vernacular, and embellishing the boring news with interesting words, etc., but it is mostly a reform of the superficial form, and the substantive reform is still less. Everyone is still just blindly indulging in low-level tastes. To be honest, low-level taste is the fatal wound of all publications. Even if it can make sales good, it often loses its fundamental meaning. It is also a very good means to slightly incline the content to taste to increase the reading interest of the shallow public; but if it is too low-level, it will still be like the old small newspapers, and it will instead apply poison to the public. Secondly, each newspaper is still like the old small newspapers, and the scope of content adopted is too narrow; praising corners and talking about prostitutes is the most inferior tendency of the old small newspapers; and the newly rising ones also still play this old tune; exposing personal privacy, creating rumors and slanders, is also the most inferior tendency of the old small newspapers, and the newly rising ones still have it. Some pay extra attention to reporting the private affairs of some celebrities and literati, and abandon the important reports of the world, the country, and the society (on this point, I think the Times Daily has the necessity of recommending it). I feel that such narrowness really cannot make people feel what is different between the newly rising and the old ones. Since there is no difference, then the destructive power mentioned above is not at all, let alone the need for construction. As a result, I am afraid that the new will eventually become the old.

I hope that people who run small newspapers can pay attention to their reforms. Especially in the sense of promoting "destruction."

Introducing Lin Yutang's Geography

— Quan Jia

Translated by Chuan Donghua / Published by New Life Bookstore

As usual, a geography book is not easy to write well. Although some people have used travelogue style to write geography, it has not achieved much success. This book is a very strange book. It is neither like a stereotyped article that makes people's heads swell when they look at it, nor does it focus on interest and ignore meaning. The purpose of this book is to let us know the relationship between humans and nature, and it does not tell us to memorize the names of mountains and rivers.

Lin Yutang himself said: "My work is all based on intellectual and humanistic points of view. I want to try to point out that "man" is more important than anything in the world - more important than religion, painting, and literature. I want to make people understand that "man" is the center of the universe!" The author, Lin Yutang, got rid of the attitude of scholars in the past. He brought knowledge out of the "study room" of experts, freed it of its feet, and went to the free road! Chuan Donghua once said in "About the Author": "This book uses the torch of humanism in the 20th century to clearly illuminate the buried culture!" Well, readers, remember this sentence and read this strange book!

For example, in the chapter about the Republic of China, he specifically mentioned the "Yellow Peril" chapter, in which he said:

"Because the Yellow River used to flow south into the Yellow Sea. But in 1852, it suddenly changed its course, but the word "flood" in Chinese means a real "flood." Since the end of the seventeenth century, the Yellow River has changed its outlet ten times. In other places, dikes can be used to prevent river breaks, but in the Yellow River and Yangtze River, dikes are not needed. For example, in 1852, the dike that broke the Yellow River was originally as high as fifty feet, but it broke through like a piece of manure paper."

In a short passage, isn't Lin Yutang already telling you a fragment of China's water disaster? He also talked about China's recent situation.

"When the aggression of foreign powers against China became too obvious, the Chinese had learned a lesson and knew that the Western countries were going to China, not with the greatest interest in the books of Confucius, but with more interest in coal, iron, and oil. China then began to realize the need to quickly engage in "Westernization" by emulating Japan.

I am not a prophet. I don't know what will happen in the next ten or fifteen years. But I expect that the situation will not change much, because China is catching up too late. But if she does catch up, then may God have mercy on us, because, cough, how will we have to pay a bill at that time, what a bill!" (See chapter 37 for the original text)

There have been two translations of Chinese before and after. One is jointly translated by Mr. Chen Shoushi and Hu Dianwei, entitled "Lin Yutang's World Geography," and the other is translated by Mr. Chuan Donghua, entitled "Our World." I cannot criticize the merits of the two, but the former is a free translation and the latter is a literal translation. In order to leave a perfect true image in the minds of readers, I chose the latter book.

(1) Opening a bookstore

The old gentleman said: "Huh! Opening a bookstore, it's only happening now!" This means that the old gentleman cannot get used to the new bookstores that publish books that are neither "classics and history" nor "collections of philosophers." Secondly, that is also true. The "trend" of "opening a bookstore" really only began around 1927. There were bookstores before, but not the new bookstores of today. There were people who opened bookstores before, but "opening a bookstore" did not become a "trend" for intellectuals.

In the past, the so-called bookstores were mainly those "Shufang (山房)" and "Shuwu (書屋)" and the like, bookstores specializing in printing old books (such as Xiaojing Shufang (校經山房), Saoye Shufang (掃葉山房), and Youzheng Shuju (有正書局), which are very famous in Shanghai), Since the Meiji Restoration, the new foreign school system was imported, and China's "schools" have also changed in nature slightly. There was a need for the printing of new textbooks, and new bookstores followed. Generated and developed, but until after the May Fourth Movement, the New Culture Movement surged up, but all the "new" bookstores were only a few such as the Commercial Press, the China Book Company, and the Civilization Book Company. Later, because the development of the Commercial Press was particularly large, except for the general gentlemen who paid attention to the version went to the old book stalls in Beiping and the book collections in various places to buy "Ming edition" and "Song edition," in the minds of general elementary school students, middle school students (and even college students), The so-called bookstore is only the Commercial Press. From this, we can see the "reality" of "bookstores."

Regardless of whether the progress of culture promotes the development of bookstores, or the development of bookstores causes the progress of culture, in short, that time was really too lonely in the cultural circle. In addition to some textbooks, the so-called social science books that don't hurt or itch, and the semi-new and semi-old novels (such as the translations represented by Lin's translations of novels and the Novel World's wildman records, etc. are also similar), go and flip through the so-called large bookstores at that time, such as the Commercial Press, the China Book Company, and the Civilization. What kind of things are there that are related to cultural promotion?

We have to praise the new impetus of the publishing industry triggered by the National Revolution! Around 1925, as far as Shanghai is concerned, new stimuli occurred in the publishing industry! Taidong did not attract everyone's attention at that time, Guanghua Book Company was established, the creation of the Creative Society Publishing Department, and the southward migration of the Beixin Book Company, for Shanghai, which was called the "publishing center" of the publishing industry, no matter what it was, several sons were thrown into the still swamp, followed by the spring tide, Nanchang, the crowd, the New Life, Kaiming, and Liming. The companies Xingqi, and then created a very popular "asking bookstore" trend. At that time, the general youth's understanding of the publishing industry changed: not only did the Commercial Press not be the only representative of the bookstore, but also the Commercial Press was equal to the previous "Shan". "Shufang" Bookstores, old book industry, and new bookstores have become three irreconcilable things. —To be continued—

Two Emergency Common Senses

— Editor

(2) Stroke

Stroke, commonly known as 中風 (zhòng fēng), is different from 卒倒 (cù dǎo, collapsing suddenly), which is in exactly the opposite position.

Stroke is caused by the rupture of blood vessels in the brain, where the blood compresses the brain tissue, or by the blockage of blood vessels, which interrupts blood flow to the brain. This condition is generally caused by hardening of the blood vessels, making them prone to rupture. There are prodromal symptoms such as numbness of the limbs, dizziness, tinnitus, and headache. People who suffer from syphilis, alcoholism, or excessive obesity due to abnormal internal endocrine function are prone to this disease. This condition is very dangerous and different from sudden collapse, posing a risk to life.

Emergency treatment before seeking medical attention: Loosen the patient's clothing and belt, and let them lie down comfortably with their head slightly elevated to reduce blood pressure. Apply cold water or an ice pack to the forehead. Those who usually take the endocrine preparation "Reproductive Element" should not suffer from this condition.

The Bargaining Between England and France

— Li Min

Ever since the Italian Blackshirt Prime Minister Mussolini resolved to conquer the black king of Abyssinia in distant East Africa, to fulfill the obligation to this "barbaric" nation—and voluntarily pay a great price—to instill the "civilization" of European whites, this incident has immediately transformed the Italian conquest of the "barbaric" nation into a dispute between England and Italy over colonies.

England's interests in African colonies and in the Mediterranean Sea are such that it must exert "nine bulls and two tigers" to maintain them; however, Germany is its only ally on the European continent. The difficulty of the problem lies in this point. Should it still contact France and jointly attack Italy? Or would it rather abandon contact with France and continue to contact Germany to jointly prepare for a larger attack on the Soviet Union than Italy? England's current diplomacy is really undecided on this point. We can clearly see where its painstaking efforts lie.

France is also cunning. On the German issue, it has always wanted to obtain England's cooperation and jointly oppress Germany, but England's answer to it has been the opposite, contacting Germany to oppress France. This situation has forced France to change its previous attitude in the past two years and contact the Soviet Union, which holds completely opposite positions. This time, the Italian expedition to Abyssinia occurred, and France hoped that this event could change England's previous attitude towards France in order to jointly sanction Italy in exchange for England's assistance in sanctioning Germany. Therefore, when England's request for France to jointly sanction Italy reached France, France put forward a precondition, saying: If Germany invades Austria, will England also help France sanction Germany? England's answer was very cunning, saying that it would depend on the situation at that time and cannot be predetermined at present (see the telegraph news in the newspaper on the 28th). France naturally felt disappointed. Therefore, whether France's future diplomatic policy is to assist England or Italy is a very interesting question.

The diplomacy between England and France is currently in such a bargaining situation. On the one hand, we have received news from the newspaper that Germany is actively preparing to attack Russia. The East is also accelerating its preparations. Perhaps when the curtain of the Second World Massacre is unfolded, the Soviet Union, which dominates Northern Europe, will become an enlarged Abyssinia under the guns of various powers.

Words of the Heart

— Simon

When the cold moonlight shines on the coconut branches, when the small grass on the tomb top falls, when the lingering smoky rain covers the mountains and seas, it is when I am facing the autumn wind and shedding tears for the tragic memories. With memories, my thoughts have been confused. I cannot clearly count whether it was last year or the year before. It has always been very long and very far away. But I still feel as vivid as if it were in front of me, which gradually turns into an incurable heart failure symptom. Linzi, I would not hesitate to use my own hands to cut my own throat and end this laborious life, so that I can lie in the underground cave with you. Only for the sake of the traction of your last few words, I am always holding the idea of not being able to let you down. In this way, I silently drag up a broken body, and three years of time have passed in a trance. Like the early autumn god

spreading the brocade on the mountains and seas, thinking that your graveyard should have another degree of desolation, and there is no shepherd's song, then you are still lonely. And I am still staying in a different place, and I can only perform a wild heart sacrifice by vaguely watching the moon on the sea head when I knock the twilight bells of the ancient church of Sakyamuni. Linzi, if you are conscious, you should be able to imagine how I am living a day more frightened than a nightmare. From that day on, my soul has been taken away by some demons at the same time, but I still don't believe that you will be able to walk so leisurely, so unencumbered, as if there is really nothing in the world worthy of your nostalgia. Linzi, definitely not, I know that you must have hidden to the ground with eternal regrets. Therefore, I know that you, the person who was mourned, must have more words in your heart than anyone else, but you finally left silently without leaving a word.

I often dream that on the distant plains, I am slightly bedridden, with sharp silver arrows running through my heart, and I seem to see the shadow of the Muhammad statue on the high tower pushed in front of me like a wall, feeling a burst of shock, and then I wake up. It turned out that I was still lying on the table, and the bleak lamp flowers were stroking my lungs, which were stretched tightly and exhaling emptiness. I suddenly found a patch of bright red blood stains dyed on my lapel, which was moist and had not dried out yet. I was not afraid at all, but deeply wondered how such a sick and frail body still had so much blood. I could not help but regret that my blood should not be shed in vain at this time. I should save it up to wait for the day to go to your grave and pour it out to my heart's content as the only sacrifice!

When the news of my imprisonment reached you, you abandoned all obstacles and difficulties, and came to this island from a distant island country after three days and nights of sea travel. Later, you used many methods to meet me. I still clearly remember that day you were wearing a plain light dress, and you looked even more like a delicate white hibiscus in the spring breeze. And what was completely unexpected was that you smiled at me with no sorrow or sadness. Because that place was not a place where you could say much, you only said briefly: "Wait, the sun will never leave you." Although it was a short sentence, your whole soul and passionate tone had moved me to tears. If I were allowed to cry out loud, I would have cried out loud at that time. My deep, dark, well-like heart was like a stone thrown into it, and countless waves suddenly surged up. Yes, Linzi, you are the sun, the forever bright sun in my heart. Without you shining, I am afraid I would have ceased to exist in this world.

My crime could only be canceled with a lot of gold. Therefore, thanks to you for selling all your gold jewelry; if it was not enough, you had to raise it everywhere in a shameful way. I finally returned to the world under the sun, but at the same time I decided to leave the sun in my heart. You, on the contrary, left the world under the sun and went to another dark world. Linzi, is the world really so bleak? Who can I tell my grievances and sorrow?

Autumn is deep, and the red hibiscus in the south will change from bright to yellow and wither. Linzi, your enthusiastic ten youthful lives, like red hibiscus, are easy to thank and flourish. Could it be that you are the incarnation of the flower demon? I carry the heavy burden of sin and human affection on my shoulders, with a tired breath, sighing, stumbling in the wind and rain, in the dark, on the boundless journey of the wilderness. I only see the spread of dark clouds, but I have never greeted the dawn. No tears, no hope, but Linzi, is your immortal soul also drifting, why can't I even chase it in my dreams?

Memories of the Ancient City

— Luo Zhihua

Camels shake "May I" all day long...

Tuning the sad elegy in the autumn wind,

Yellow sand, yellow leaves,

Lining the loneliness in the lonely heart.

Although I have been to ×× for three years, there is always a shadow of an ancient city in my deep memory! There are buildings with historical and cultural value, blending with the vast desert, in this ancient city - Kaifeng, just like a dead curtain, there is no trace of vitality, urban atmosphere: but, I miss that place very much, the above poem was written three years ago in the summer when I missed my friends in Kaifeng. - I love it there, I love the simplicity and loyalty of the lives of the people there.

Speaking of Guanfeng, I think of Beiping.

Before I went to Beiping, I had dreamed of the situation in Beiping, and most of my imagination was exaggerated too much, so I thought that there must be: camels shaking their dumb copper bells, walking in the desert, its quietness is like a wanderer. At the same time, on the desolate streets, only the sound of the wooden fish of the old monks floated out of the temple and echoed. Other than that, it was all loneliness, the loneliness of death.

However, one autumn, when I walked out of the "Qianmen Station," everything was not as I imagined. Most of these imaginations were related to living in Kaifeng.

Kaifeng is indeed an ancient city.

Xiangguo Temple, Yuwangtai, Iron Pagoda, and Longting all retain their ancient flavor.

However, it has also been gradually invaded by modern civilization.

For example, Xiangguo Temple, its content is similar to the Tianqiao in Beiping and the Chenghuang Temple in Shanghai. It is a place of entertainment for the petty bourgeoisie. In the past, many things were stored in the temple halls. After the Northern Expedition, they all became general people's clubs. No one knows how many people play here every day, and no one knows how many people are happy. The Northern Expedition revived Xiangguo Temple.

Longting, it was the old palace of the Song Dynasty. If you walk to the heights of this palace and look around on a dusk, you can't help but think of the nobility of the emperor. At that time, he could look at the vast land and the boundless fog in the distance. The reason why he wanted to build the palace so high was also to demonstrate to the people. Layers of steps represent layers of official ranks. He sat on the magnificent hall at the end of the steps, making everyone admire him; the indigenous people said, "The emperor sits on the Jinluan Hall, and the governor can only meet in the Wu Chao Gate! - I dare not lift my head"!

After the Northern Expedition, it was also made public. Many fantasies were broken.

The Iron Pagoda is even a great building. It is all built of glazed tiles, thirteen levels high, and the outside is exposed to the sun, reflecting green, purple, and red light. From the highest level, you can see the long body of the Yellow River like a jade belt.

Yuwangtai, although it has been abandoned, still retains its natural beauty.

My childhood was completely lost in this ancient city. And this ancient city has cultivated my character to be so melancholy. Every time I think of my hometown, I first remember the suffering of the floods, and then I think of this city.

Night Crossing

— Shen Wu

As I passed Ox Head Ridge, the sky gradually darkened. Looking back at the layers of mountain shadows, and the clusters of wild trees, the undergrowth, and the pine forest, the surrounding scenery was bleak and gloomy. Even if one had a gourd-sized胆子 (courage), one couldn't help but tremble in one's heart; moreover, the bandits here were even more ferocious than the large stronghold on the skirt of Mountain Dai.

Eight legs moved ever more closely on the winding mountain road, the bamboo sandals scraping against the mud and sand with "sha suo," "sha suo" sounds. Everyone seemed to complain that the sky was getting dark too quickly: "Damn it, we haven't even reached Black Water Ferry yet." However, no matter what, our pace couldn't get much faster. The more anxious we felt, the less energy we had to walk. I wondered if we were bewitched by some ghost? In the past, we would cross the Black Water before the sun even set, but today we only just passed Ox Head Ridge. Wouldn't it be three watches later before we got home?

Turning around a winding path surrounded by wild brambles, I shifted the pole from my left shoulder to my right. At that moment, I suddenly felt a bit of pain in my shoulder. I reached back to rub it, then forced myself to keep walking. I had walked almost a whole day, and I gradually felt that the load was indeed much heavier than usual. No wonder Old Song was complaining this morning that the goods were piled up more and more, while I sleepily rubbed my bleary eyes and didn't say a word, so I was taken advantage of again...

By the time we reached that dark, deep river, the moon had already poked its head out from behind the mountains. The riverbank was covered with another thicket of dense weeds. Some sounded like frogs, but not quite, making "ge la," "ge la" noises in the grass.

Looking at the ferry landing, it seemed there were no lights. Er Lin became quite anxious and shouted loudly at the boatman, "Hey! Bastard!" But Old Zhu stopped him short:

"Stupid pig, are you trying to sell us out to the enemy? Shouting so loud!...Better go closer to the dock and take a look."

Everyone also complained a little about Er Lin's recklessness.

As we approached the ferry landing, the boat was indeed not moored there. Looking across the river, there was no sign of it either. The moon was hazy, only illuminating the turbulent flow of the dark water like a sandy shoal. The sound of the river mingled with the chirping of insects in the mountains, very clear and pleasant.

We put down our loads, and our hearts truly grew anxious. Everyone looked at each other in dismay. Er Lin glared at Old Zhu, as if seeking revenge.

"Where did that dog's bastard go with the boat? Pig—" Although he was still angrily cursing, his voice was much lower, so only the few of us here could hear him.

The night was silent and vast. Amidst the alarm and anxiety, Old Song was the most able to remain calm. He shone his flashlight around the river surface, and a beam of white light swept across the weeds by the riverbank. Sure enough, under a large black rock, we saw the small ferry boat. Only then did everyone smile and pick up their loads, heading toward the rock wall. The weeds rustled as we moved through them.

"Pig, aren't you going to carry our goods? You pig's get, still sleeping?..."

Old Zhu shone his flashlight on the boatman's face, and he slowly rubbed his eyes and lit the oil lamp. Several people threw the goods into the boat's cabin, and Er Lin alone collapsed on the deck, dozing off.

The boat swayed into the middle of the river in the fast-flowing Black Water. The hull gradually swayed a little uneasily.

"Hey, pig, steer carefully, don't send your ancestors to their graves!"

Everyone watched the turbulent river with anxious hearts. The moon slowly climbed up the mountain peak.

Page 23

Wind

— Xiong Zilei

A season of drifting, a September of drifting, a September night of drifting. I often walk by the quiet lake, watching the pale lamplight floating on the water, my heart shrouded in fog as I think.

Gleaming stars, blending with the serene moon, everything is steeped in melancholy. The wind, blowing from the distant north, brings a whispered farewell of falling leaves, heralding the arrival of autumn!

I gazed towards the direction the wind was blowing for a long time; however, I found nothing. I could only close my eyes and listen quietly to the wind's playing.

This rhythm-less music made me recall many old days, made me depict many old joys and sorrows. Wind that makes one wither and fade!

I look at my shadow printed on the ground, enough to confuse me; however, when the wind blows, even the shadow sways! Am I entering another world of old age?

Ah, everything is aging in the playing of the wind!

I return with sorrowful steps.

Broadcast Program

New Song Introduction

The Washing Song

A song from Shanghai Sound Film "Peach Blossom Dream"

The clear water flows and flows, flowing over the shallows and over the bridge. The shallows' water plays a musical tune, the women under the bridge sing high. Sister Zhang comes early, all kinds of clothes float on the water. Sister-in-law Li comes early, all kinds of clothes spread on the stones. This year is really not good, not warm enough to wear, not full enough to eat. We wear torn pants with ragged coats, eat pancakes with fried dough sticks. Everyone is diligent and frugal without worries, enduring and persevering.

The clear water flows gently and slowly, some families are happy, some are sad. The happy ones enjoy themselves enough, the sorrowful ones are lonely and sad. Sister Zhang holds hands, holding the hands of a flowery good friend. Sister-in-law Li has an ugly temper, her unemployed husband has gone away to work. This year is really not free, money is not stable, love doesn't last long. We wear shiny satin with bright silk, eat big fish with fatty meat. It harms the poor, hard to find a partner, the rich can embrace anyone they like.

The clear water flows and flows, some are carefree, some are busy. The carefree ones idly wander and sway, the busy ones panic with no destination. Sister Zhang thinks all day about following a rich, white-haired man. Sister-in-law Li thinks all day about winning the first prize in the aviation lottery. This year, if one runs out of food, one won't live long. We wear pawn tickets, selling everything we can, eat mixed swill with thin soup. Everyone is finding ways to relieve the disaster, to avoid the poor dying out completely.

Film

Kaige's Behind-the-Scenes Drama

— Bai Mu

This is an old story, but not too old, and very interesting, so I will mention it here.

A week or ten days ago, the Yihua "Kaige" photography crew went to Suzhou to shoot outdoor scenes. The first day's work location was Liuyuan Garden. Liuyuan is the best-known garden in Wu, with excellent scenery, and is the only leisure destination for Suzhou gentry and women. The garden has a lotus pond, which is very wide. Although the lotus flowers have withered, the green leaves are still lush. Therefore, they ordered a paper flower shop to specially make hundreds of lotus flowers tied to the skeletons, no less than the reappearance of the lotus blooming season.

Because on that day, no fewer than hundreds of people came to sightsee in admiration of Yuan Meiyun's fame, and the scene was to shoot Yuan Meiyun and Sun Zeyi rowing a boat in the pool for several shots, the new photographer Wu Weiyun had to go into the pool to work. However, the pool water was dirty and unbearable, and the bottom of the pool was nauseating mud. Moreover, although the sun was out, the weather was very cold, so when he finished shooting several shots, his lips had turned bronze, and he was "ge ge" chattering. However, to show his bravery, he simply swam to the shore, struggling to climb ashore, but he was exhausted and couldn't climb up. At this time, among the many spectators, a friend holding a camera kindly ran to drag him, but he couldn't win, and he fell into the pool in a very excellent diving posture. Both of them were covered in mud and each tasted a few mouthfuls of stinky water. As a result, that friend quietly went to receive Bu Wancang's brandy treat amidst the laughter of the entire garden.

Wei Heling in "The Storm" and Shu Xiuwen in "Night Fragrance" gave me a fresher and deeper impression in these two films than the leading actors Yuan Meiyun and Hu Die. People with stage experience are ultimately better at "getting into character" than those without cultivation. One cannot help but increasingly believe

Publishing World

Chang Sheng Weekly, published by Sanhe Publishing House at 138 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, decided to resume publishing a special extra-large issue on the first of each month starting last month. It is said that issue 40, that is, the special extra-large issue on the 10th, has been published today. In terms of text, there are dozens of articles such as "Liquidation of Yihua Company's Accounts," "Yuan Meiyun's Life and Recent Living Conditions," and "The Chen Diao Engagement Case Dispute Has Not Ended." In terms of copper plates, there are Chen Yanyan's cover and multiple photos of major stars. Retail price is only one dime.

Linglong is the first women's magazine created in the country, emphasizing both pictures and text, with novel editing. Each issue has articles commenting on women's issues, and introductions to common sense for housewives. Other columns such as mailbox, movies, literature and art, ancient and modern scandals, and women's news are also opened. Retail price is one dime per copy. Subscription for the whole year of fifty issues is five yuan. And you can get a 20% discount.
